There is no on-page reconciliation; there is, by strong inference, at least one long phone call and at least one in-person off-record conversation in which both behaved as the people they had been before the rupture, and afterward returned to their separate lives without converting the contact into a resumption.

**Psychological signature, this period.** The moral-injury structure flagged in §4 reactivates under M-Day pressure in a specific way: she is now reporting on the *near-extinction* of the population she once helped panic against (through Legacy). The file flags this as the period in which her **subclinical adjustment-disorder-with-depressed-mood substrate likely deepens**, without crystallizing into a treatable episode. She does not seek therapy in any record the file possesses, and the inference is that she has not — a person of her ethical seriousness and intellectualization-dominant defenses tends to **read therapy as something other people need**, particularly when her grief is something she has chosen to keep.

---

## 4. The Initiative / Utopia / Schism Years

Through the late 2000s and early 2010s the mutant-affairs beat becomes politically tractable in ways it never was before: registration-equivalent policy under the Fifty-State Initiative, the consolidation on Utopia, the eventual Schism. Subject's footprint in the corpus during this stretch is the lightest of her published life — a few panels, a few referenced segments, a name on a chyron. The file reads this as **deliberate professional retreat from the front of the camera**, not displacement:

- She is by this point in her late forties to early fifties (the corpus has never firmly fixed her birth year; the file places her birth in the early-to-mid 1960s based on professional seniority at first appearance).
- She has the institutional standing to send younger correspondents into the field while she anchors, edits, or contributes analytically.
- She has the personal motivation — proximity to Utopia coverage means proximity to Hank's current life, which she has consistently managed by *titration*, not avoidance.

**The acquisition of a cat, inferred.** Somewhere in this stretch the file places, with low-to-moderate confidence, the entry of a domestic animal into her apartment. The basis is the cadence of single professional women of her demographic, the absence of any other domestic presence, and a single late background detail in a cameo panel (an item on a counter consistent with pet ownership). This is the kind of detail a real surveillance file would log and a fictional one should infer: the **first stable cohabitant since Hank**, on her terms, low demands, present when she comes home.

**Romantic record, this period.** None on-page. The file's inference is that she has had occasional dating activity in a low-investment register — likely a recurring not-quite-relationship with a colleague or a source-adjacent professional (a foundation officer, a beat-adjacent academic, an editor at a competitor) of the kind that meets for dinner every six to ten weeks, sleeps over occasionally, and is structurally incapable of becoming a partnership because **neither party is auditioning for one**. This is consistent with a woman who has decided, without melodrama, that the partnership-shaped slot in her life is closed.

---

## 5. The 2010s Mutant-Beat Convulsions

The Avengers vs. X-Men conflict, the resurrection of the mutant population, the Inhumans-vs-mutants Terrigen crisis, and the various status quo shifts of the mid-2010s are all stories her beat would have led. She is named in passing in the corpus during several of these and shown in glimpse during one or two press-pool scenes. The file infers:

- A **shift in her on-camera persona** during this period toward what older broadcast journalists call "voice of god" register — slower cadence, more declarative, the warmth dialed down in favor of authority. This is age-appropriate and career-appropriate; it also reflects the deepening of the moral-injury substrate, which over decades tends to produce exactly this kind of affective flattening *on the public surface* even when interior life is unchanged.

- **A book**, possibly two, inferred from the cadence of a reporter of her seniority and signature beat: a long-form treatment of the mutant century, likely framed as a memoir-of-witness rather than a pure history (she is too self-aware to write the latter without the former). The file places at least one such book in the late 2010s, modestly reviewed, well-respected within the press and within mutant-affairs scholarly circles, not a bestseller. The chapter on Legacy — *which she would not be able to write without addressing the disclosure* — is the chapter the file would seek to obtain, because it is the only place she has likely committed her reflective position on the rupture to durable text.

---

## 6. The Krakoan Era

The establishment of the Krakoan mutant nation-state and the radical reconfiguration of mutant-human relations is the largest mutant-affairs story since Decimation, possibly since the team's first emergence. Subject would have covered it. The file infers her posture:

- **Skeptical-engaged.** She is not a celebrant — her ethical instincts run against ethnostate-shaped solutions even when she sympathizes with their causes — and she is not a denouncer. Her coverage frame would be: *what does this mean, on the ground, for the people in it*. This is the same frame she has held since the late 1980s; the consistency is the point.
- **Re-contact with Hank in his Krakoan/X-Force capacity**, which during this period included intelligence-and-paramilitary work whose ethical character she would have found alarming. The file flags this as the **third tender encounter window** and the most morally fraught of the post-rupture record: she is now in a position to *expose Hank's work* in a way that would harm him professionally and politically, and she has not. Whether by ethical judgment (she does not have the sourcing), by residual loyalty (probable), or by the recognition that the public-interest calculus is genuinely ambiguous (likely), she has held. This is itself a development. The woman who broke Legacy without warning him has, in late career, learned to **hold a story while she decides what the story is**.
- **Recognition that she is now an elder of her beat.** Younger mutant-affairs correspondents come to her for backgrounding; she has likely mentored at least one whose byline is now larger than hers in the corpus. This satisfies the *being-of-use to a public* drive identified in §5 in a sustainable register.

---

## 7. Current State (Present Tense)

The file's best read of the present:

**Location.** Same apartment. Same neighborhood. She has not left New York and will not.

**Vocation.** Senior correspondent / contributor role at her network, mutant-affairs portfolio retained as signature, with rotating analytical and long-form responsibilities. Possibly a podcast or limited-series-documentary side venture (this is what a journalist of her vintage and standing does in the present media economy and the file infers it with moderate confidence). Salary comfortable, not extravagant. No financial distress in the record or by inference.

**Physical condition.** Late fifties to early sixties. The somatic baseline established in §2 of the shared assessment — unremarkable, durable, well-maintained — continues. She walks more than she used to (the field has been replaced by the city), eats with mild discipline, drinks at the social adult level, sleeps approximately six hours and considers it sufficient. The first age-related medical events (a perimenopausal stretch in the 2010s navigated without commentary, a routine but inconvenient orthopedic issue, a screening or two that came back clean) are inferred and unremarkable. She is healthy in the way working adults are healthy until they aren't.

**Domestic life.** Solitary, structured, not lonely in the clinical sense. Pet present. Books, broadcast, work-from-home capacity, a small set of standing engagements (a Tuesday dinner with one or two long-tenured friends, a Saturday morning routine that includes the print edition of at least one newspaper she still receives on paper because *of course she does*).

**Relational life.** No partner. No active dating in any sustained sense. A small dense network of long-tenured colleagues and a smaller set of close friends, most of whom she has known since the late 1980s or 1990s. **No children**, no nieces or nephews in active proximity in the record, no extended family routinely in scene — the file infers parents deceased or distant, possibly a sibling somewhere with whom she has cordial holiday contact and not much more. This is the relational footprint of a person whose **chosen family is her colleagues and her work**.

**Hank.** Indeterminate, given the volatility of his recent record (his Krakoan-era ethical degradation, the Reilly Brown / Ben Percy *X-Force* arc, the eventual reckoning, the resurrection complications). The file's strongest inference is that she has **watched his recent trajectory with grief that is no longer in any way romantic** — a grief for the man she knew rather than for the relationship — and that she has neither contacted him nor written about him in any extended way during his worst period, on the principle that her relationship to his story disqualifies her from being its narrator. When the corpus eventually permits a clean Hank, she will likely interview him once, and that interview will be careful, warm, and final.

**Psychological state.** Stable, contained, and operating in the long key the moral-injury substrate produced thirty years ago. She is **not depressed** in any clinical sense; she is *settled* in a register most of her colleagues would mistake for contentment and a few who know her well would recognize as something quieter and more permanent. The contradiction she elected to live in (§5, *Synthesized read*) has become the architecture of her life rather than its pressure. She does not think about Legacy daily. She thinks about it when it is invoked, and the thinking is now a habit, not a wound that reopens. This is the closest a person of her defenses gets to peace.

**What she is doing right now, on a representative weekday.** Up early. Coffee. Wires. A morning call with a producer about a segment. A working lunch she will half-eat. An interview in the afternoon with someone in mutant-affairs policy — younger than she is, deferential without being obsequious, aware they are talking to a person who has been on this beat longer than they have been alive. An edit session in the late afternoon. Home by eight. The cat. The late broadcast on in the background. A book on the arm of the chair. Lights out by midnight. She is exactly where she expected to end up, and the only thing she did not expect was that being exactly where she expected to end up would feel, on balance, **acceptable**.

That acceptability — earned, unsentimental, faintly elegiac, and entirely her own — is the current state of the file.


## Medical History

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: TRISH TILBY
## Section 3 — MEDICAL HISTORY

### Preliminary Note

The medical record on Subject is, paradoxically, one of the most informative in the X-corpus precisely because of what it does not contain. Subject is a baseline-human civilian woman, b. circa late 1950s by published-age inference (presented as mid-thirties through the late-1980s appearances, consistent with a network correspondent rank achieved by that decade of life), with no mutation, no augmentation, no surgical-cosmetic intervention of record, no chronic disease state, and no documented hospitalization across more than a decade of continuous appearance in environments that routinely kill or maim other civilians. A standard intelligence file on a comparable beat reporter — war correspondent, organized-crime reporter, mutant-affairs correspondent — would by the same career-tenure show stress fractures, a substance-use entry, at least one stitch line, likely a concussion, and a divorce-adjacent therapy course. Subject's chart instead resembles that of a healthy academic. This is not luck. It is **competence rendered as physiology**: the absence of injury is itself the medical finding.

What follows is granular to the limit of inference.

---

### 1. Constitutional / Baseline Physiology

- **Sex/Karyotype:** Female, presumed 46,XX, no record of intersex variation or endocrine anomaly.
- **Age cohort:** Adult throughout the record; estimated 33–45 across the principal appearance window. No on-panel acknowledgment of perimenopausal symptomatology, though the late-canon flatness of affect could be partially explained by mid-life endocrine shift (low-confidence; psychological causation is sufficient).
- **Habitus:** Slim-to-medium build, on-camera-conforming proportions (occupationally selected); height inferred at approximately 5'6"–5'8" against panel-comparison with McCoy in pre-secondary-mutation form. Musculature consistent with moderate cardiovascular activity and the carriage-strain of fieldwork (lights, cabling, occasional camera-assist); no athletic-development signature.
- **Hair/eyes:** Brunette (depicted dark brown, occasionally rendered black under print-stock variation); eye color rendered variably blue/green by colorist drift, most consistent reading green. No graying depicted within the principal window — likely cosmetic management, standard for on-air talent.
- **Dentition:** Apparently intact, well-aligned, network-orthodontic standard. No tooth loss, no visible restoration. Likely a privileged-childhood orthodontic course in the late 1960s/early 1970s, inferred from outcome.
- **Skin:** Fair, no significant scarring on uncovered surfaces (face, neck, hands, forearms in dinner-scene depictions). The hands are particularly notable — a beat reporter who has spent a decade-plus in crisis environments and has *no* visible hand trauma (knuckle scars, burn keloids, lateral palm scarring from falls) has been disciplined about hand-protective field behavior. She picks her shots.
- **Voice:** Network-trained chest-resonant alto, no audible nodular pathology across the record despite vocal-load occupational demand. Likely benefits from coaching and from a non-shouter's temperament — she cuts through by precision, not volume, which is protective of the vocal folds.

### 2. Pediatric / Pre-Career (Inferred)

No canonical record, but standard reconstruction:

- **Vaccinations:** Complete to U.S. middle-class childhood standard of cohort (smallpox scar likely on upper deltoid from the pre-1972 cohort); MMR, polio, DPT, later occupational hepatitis-B series likely added at network onboarding.
- **Childhood illness:** No referenced history. Inferred unremarkable — varicella likely (pre-vaccine cohort), routine otitis course.
- **Orthopedic:** No referenced fractures. Posture and gait in field-coverage panels show no compensatory asymmetry consistent with un-reduced childhood injury.
- **Allergies:** None of record. Inferred none of clinical significance — she works in environments (combustion, smoke, post-blast particulate at Genosha and Onslaught coverage) that would unmask reactive airway disease, and shows no symptomatology.
- **Vision:** Apparently uncorrected during fieldwork. Possible contact-lens use undepicted; possible mild refractive error compensated by teleprompter sizing. No spectacles of record.

### 3. Occupational Exposure History

This is the medically active section of the file. By beat and tenure, Subject has accumulated exposures that in any other civilian would generate a chronic-care chart.

- **Smoke/particulate:** Repeated post-incident reporting at sites of mutant/anti-mutant violence — building fires (Genoshan civic violence period), urban combat debris (Onslaught NYC aftermath), Sentinel-incident particulate (Operation: Zero Tolerance coverage). Estimated cumulative inhalation exposure comparable to a moderate-tenure urban firefighter without respirator discipline. Subject shows **no cough, no exertional dyspnea, no clubbing**. Either a robust constitutional pulmonary reserve, fortunate wind direction across many incidents, or — most likely — disciplined field positioning (upwind, perimeter, ducks back when ash falls). The behavioral evidence supports the third.
- **Energy / radiological:** Proximity to mutant energy discharges (Apocalypse-era plasma events, Onslaught psionic field), Sentinel weapons-fire, the residual unknowns of the Legacy investigation. No radiation-illness sequelae. The Marvel-universe physics of "mutant energy" does not map cleanly to ionizing radiation, but a real-world intelligence file would flag the cumulative-unknown-exposure category and recommend baseline thyroid and CBC monitoring. None of record.
- **Biological:** *The single defining exposure event.* During investigation and reportage of the Legacy Virus cross-over story she was, by definition, in proximity to infected materials, infected patients, and infected handlers. She did not contract the disease (her published record continues post-disclosure with no morbidity). The clinical implication is significant: either she practiced rigorous PPE/standoff discipline beyond what the panel depicts, or her exposure was less direct than her reportage implied, or the cross-species transmission vector was narrower than initially feared. The intelligence inference: she behaved as a journalist who **understood biohazard protocol** — gowning at MacTaggert's facility, distance from bedside, no specimen handling. This is consistent with the general pattern of disciplined field behavior.
- **Auditory:** Repeated proximity to explosive ordnance, energy discharge, Sentinel footfall. No hearing-aid in late canon; no requests for repeats in dialogue. Probable mild high-frequency notch by mid-forties consistent with cohort and exposure — undetected/uncomplained-of.
- **Psychiatric exposure:** Repeated witness to mass-casualty events, deceased children (Legacy storyline), violent death of sources. Treated separately in the Psychiatric section; the somatic correlates one would expect — startle-elevation, hypervigilance signs, sleep architecture disruption — are not depicted. Either suppressed under camera, or genuinely well-regulated. The consistent absence across years of panel suggests the latter.

### 4. Acute Injury Record

- **No fractures of record.**
- **No surgical scars of record.**
- **No documented concussion.** A baseline civilian who has been in blast-proximate scenes without a concussion entry has either been remarkably lucky or has cultivated the field reflex of getting low and behind structure. Subject is shown doing exactly this in multiple coverage panels.
- **Minor lacerations / contusions** are plausible but not explicitly canonized; treat as inferred-routine. The reporter's hand-cut and knee-bruise are below depiction threshold and would not generate a chart entry.
- **Heat / cold exposure:** Coverage in extreme environments (Muir Island, the Antarctic peripheries of the Savage Land mutant-affairs traffic) implies thermal-stress days. No frostbite, no heatstroke of record. Standard cold-weather field kit assumed.

The **clean acute-trauma record is the central somatic finding**. It indexes the personality directly: she is a journalist who accepts proximity but rejects heroics. She does not run toward fire to be seen running toward fire. She positions, observes, withdraws.

### 5. Reproductive / Sexual Health

- **Menarche, contraception, gynecologic care:** Off-panel, presumed routine and adequately resourced.
- **Pregnancies:** None of record. **Termination history:** none of record. **Fertility status:** unspecified and likely undetermined by Subject herself; the question never arose in a relational frame that demanded an answer.
- **STI screening:** Inferred routine to a sexually active urban professional of cohort, particularly in the AIDS-aware late-1980s milieu where she came of professional age. The Subject of her own most consequential story (a pandemic crossover virus) would have been keenly attentive to her own seroprevalence as both citizen and reporter.
- **Sexual partner of long duration: Henry P. McCoy.** The medical aspect of this relationship is unusual enough to warrant explicit note. McCoy across the relationship's duration is **anatomically and physiologically nonhuman in multiple respects** — fur-covered integument, increased musculoskeletal mass and torque capacity, dentition with significantly enlarged canines, dermal callusing on knuckle and foot pad consistent with knuckle-walking gait, body temperature and metabolic rate elevated above human baseline. Sexual partnership with such a body requires the partner to have integrated, at minimum: thermoregulatory tolerance during contact (he runs hot), pressure/force calibration (his unguarded grip can break bone), fur-related dermal considerations (shed, occlusion, possible follicular reactions), and the dental geometry of intimate contact. The record's depiction of the relationship as somatically *unremarkable* — cooking together, sharing a bed, ordinary physical affection without flinch — is the strongest single piece of evidence in the file for Subject's **absence of somatic disgust reflex**. This is not a small finding. The xenophobic reflex that the broader culture in her universe weaponizes against mutants is, at root, a somatic-disgust response. She does not have it, or has trained it out, or has subordinated it permanently to her cognitive-ethical processing. Either way, the body-knowledge sits in her chart: she has slept next to a body the rest of her species was being taught to fear, and her sleep was undisturbed.
- **Post-rupture sexual history:** Sparse, inferred-minimal. The brief newsroom-orbit involvements gestured at in late canon do not develop. Whether this represents libidinal contraction (consistent with the prolonged grief picture), opportunity contraction (consistent with workaholism), or elected celibacy (consistent with unresolved attachment to McCoy) cannot be distinguished from the record. All three may be true in admixture.

### 6. Substance History

- **Alcohol:** Light-to-moderate social use, documented in dinner-scene context (wine with meals, occasional cocktail). No depiction of intoxication, no functional impairment, no morning-after scenes. Inferred consumption: 3–7 drinks/week in stable periods, possibly elevated to 7–10 in the immediate post-Legacy-disclosure months (clinical inference, not panel-documented). No suggestion of alcohol use disorder.
- **Tobacco:** None of record. Unusual for a journalist of her generational cohort; suggests she came up in the post-newsroom-smoking transition or was constitutionally non-smoking. Vocal-fold preservation supports this.
- **Caffeine:** Inferred high — broadcast cadence requires it. Coffee/tea props recur. No clinical sequelae.
- **Prescription:** None of record. The absence of a sleep aid in the post-disclosure period is notable. Either she does not use one (high tolerance for insomnia, or no insomnia), or she uses one off-camera. The cleaner inference, given her intellectualization-dominant defense structure, is that she **prefers conscious endurance to chemical intervention** — taking a sleeping pill would be an acknowledgment of an emotional wound her ego organization is committed to handling cognitively.
- **Illicit:** None of record. Inferred none. The deontological-ethical signature in her professional life makes recreational illegality a poor fit; this is not a woman who is comfortable being on the wrong side of any rule she has not personally argued her way past.

### 7. Transformations / Disabilities / Surgeries

- **Transformations:** None. She is, across the entire record, the same person in the same body. In a universe where transformation is the dominant narrative engine, this is itself a characterological statement — she is the **fixed point**.
- **Disabilities:** None of record, congenital or acquired.
- **Surgeries:** None of record. No cosmetic intervention depicted (no rhinoplastic signature, no lid-lift evidence at the appropriate cohort age). On-air career sustained without surgical maintenance suggests either fortunate genetics, disciplined non-surgical care, or both.
- **Reproductive surgery:** None of record. No depicted hysterectomy, tubal procedure, or related intervention.
- **Dental:** Inferred routine prophylactic; no major restorative work depicted.

### 8. Psychological Impact of the Somatic Record

This is the section that matters and that a pure-medical reading would miss.

**The clean chart is the platform of the personality.** Subject has no body-based identity scaffolding and, equally, no body-based shame. She has not been transformed against her will, has not had a power emerge and remake her social position, has not lost a limb, has not survived a disease that would teach her she is fragile. Her self-concept is therefore built entirely from **what she does and how well she does it** — verbal performance, ethical positioning, professional access — rather than from what she *is* in any somatic register. This produces several downstream effects:

1. **Equanimity around extraordinary bodies.** Because her own body is not an identity-bearing artifact, the dramatic bodies around her (McCoy's fur and fang, the visible mutations of her sources and subjects) do not register as identity-threats by contrast. She does not need her humanness to be the norm. She experiences McCoy's body as *his*, not as *not-hers*. This is rare.

2. **Vulnerability to identity-threats that operate in the cognitive-ethical register.** Conversely, because her self is built from competence and ethical positioning, attacks on those vectors — being lied to by an intimate, being made complicit in a suppression, being congratulated for the act that destroyed her relationship — land with the disorganizing force that a physical trauma would land for someone else. The Legacy disclosure was, in somatic terms, her **only major injury**, and it occurred entirely within the ethical-relational field.

3. **Absence of the body-as-comfort modality.** Many people, under chronic grief, find regulation through somatic self-care — exercise, food, touch, sleep architecture. Subject is not depicted using these as regulation channels. Her body is not where she lives; she lives in language and judgment. Under chronic grief, this means she has fewer of the ordinary buffers; the grief has fewer channels to drain into, which contributes to its persistence in the subclinical-but-unremitting pattern.

4. **Field discipline as character expression, not training overlay.** Her survival across exposures is not a trained reflex layered over a reckless temperament; it is the somatic expression of the same personality structure that runs her ethics — measured, deliberate, frame-first. She does not get hurt for the same reason she does not lie: because she has thought about the structure of the situation before she has entered it.

5. **The body as instrument, not subject.** Voice, presence, on-camera composure — these are tools. She maintains them (vocal use, weight, sleep enough to function) the way a violinist maintains an instrument: care without sentiment. This explains the absence of vanity behaviors and the equal absence of self-neglect behaviors. The instrument must function; beyond that, it is not the point.

### 9. Summary Clinical Impression

A baseline-human adult female of unremarkable constitutional medicine, with an occupationally exposed history that ought to have produced more chart entries than it did and didn't because Subject's behavioral discipline in hazardous environments is high. No transformations, no surgeries, no chronic disease, no substance pathology, no reproductive medical history of consequence. The single somatically-coded fact of consequence in the entire record is a *negative* finding — the absence of disgust response toward an intimate partner whose body the surrounding culture is being taught to fear — which is best read as evidence of an unusual cognitive-ethical integration capacity rather than as a medical observation per se.

The body, in Subject's case, is a clean page. Everything written on her is written elsewhere.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS: TRISH TILBY

*The body as longitudinal evidence. What twenty years of camera-facing work and ambient observation would have recorded.*

---

## 1. BASELINE PHYSICAL PRESENCE

**Build and carriage.** Mid-height (5'7"–5'8" range, as scaled against Hank McCoy and standard X-Factor newsroom figures), wiry-athletic without obvious gym signature — the build of someone who walks twelve miles a day in city blocks and stairs and treats elevators as a courtesy to others. Shoulder width slightly above norm for frame; collarbones prominent; deltoids defined enough to suggest she carries her own equipment when crews are thin. No surgical scarring visible at neckline, hands, or hairline under broadcast lighting. Skin tone reads as fair-to-medium with the season-cycling variation of someone whose work is outdoor-frequent but never tropical-long; faint tan-line ghosts at watchband and sunglasses bridge in summer footage.

**Hands.** Long-fingered, neat, unringed (notably so even during the Hank cohabitation period — no engagement signal ever shown). Nails kept short, filed not bitten, unpolished or pale neutral for camera; cuticles slightly ragged on right thumb (worry tell, see §5). Right index finger shows the faint lateral callus of decades pressing a pen against the second knuckle, supplemented in the 1990s by the corresponding thumb-pad thickening of repeated mobile-phone keypad use. Small white scar across the meaty base of the left thumb — origin unrecorded, likely kitchen, consistent with the cooking scenes during the Hank period.

**Face at rest.** Default expression carries roughly 15° more brow-engagement than American conversational baseline — the "listening face" of someone whose paycheck depends on having heard correctly. Mouth at rest neutral-to-slightly-pursed; jaw mobile (she swallows often when thinking, a small tell that distinguishes attention from boredom). Eyes wide-set, lid aperture above average — she does not squint when reading at distance, suggesting either corrected vision early or genuinely sharp acuity; no glasses visible in the record except occasional reading-half-frames at her desk in late-period appearances.

**Hair.** Brown, shoulder-length through most of the canonical period, cut to fall cleanly to the jaw at the front so it can be tucked without bobby pins for broadcast. Texture fine-to-medium, prone to weather-sensitivity (visible humidity-curl in field stand-ups from Genosha, visible static in winter NYC exteriors). Cut maintained at six-week intervals consistent with on-air talent contract standard. No coloring visible until late record, when scattered grays appear at the temples and are not concealed — a small deliberate choice, given the industry.

**Voice.** Mezzo, deliberately placed forward in the mask for broadcast clarity; conversational register sits a full third lower than her on-air voice and carries more glottal texture. She speaks at roughly 165–180 words per minute in interview, which is brisk but inside the band where listeners still feel led rather than rushed. Sentences end on a slight terminal downstep (declarative confidence) rather than the up-tick that became journalistic fashion in the late 1990s — she resists that drift visibly.

---

## 2. GAIT, POSTURE, KINESPHERE

**Gait.** Heel-strike confident, stride length about 5% longer than average for height — a quick walker who lengthens further when chasing a source down a corridor. Arms swing contralaterally and freely; she does not clutch her notebook to her chest while walking (a tell of insecure reporters), but carries it low at hip-side in the left hand, pen clipped, recorder in coat pocket on the right. Heels in studio (low block, never stiletto — she needs to be able to run); flats or low boots in field. In crowd movement she favors edges and seams, threading rather than parting; she shoulders no one and is shouldered rarely because she reads vector early.

**Standing.** Weight distributed 60/40 onto whichever foot is closer to her interlocutor, slight forward lean of the upper torso (10–15°) — the open posture of an active listener. She does not cross her arms in conversation; when she does cross them, it is a state-change signal (see §5, threat response). Hand placement at rest: one in coat pocket, the other holding the recorder or notebook; she does not gesticulate idly. When she gestures, it is to demarcate — a flat-palm horizontal sweep for "let me be clear," a pinched thumb-and-finger for precision points, an open upturned palm for invitation to elaborate.

**Sitting.** Forward in the chair, rarely using the backrest in interview; spine long, ankles often crossed under the chair (not knees). In her own office or apartment, posture decays markedly — feet on furniture, knees up, legs folded — a strong on-duty/off-duty postural switch that is itself diagnostic of someone who consciously performs containment at work.

**Kinesphere.** Personal-space bubble approximately 80 cm in casual, collapsible to 30 cm in interview when she wants to register sincerity or pressure; she leans *in* rather than reaching, which keeps her core mobile. She does not touch sources. She touches Hank constantly during the cohabitation period — palm on forearm, palm on chest, hand at the small of his back — in a manner that reads as both affection and orientation, the way a sighted person might keep light contact with a partner in a dark room.

---

## 3. FACIAL MICROPATTERNS

**The listening face.** Eyebrows raised approximately 3–5 mm above baseline, head tilted right by 8–12° (consistent left-ear-forward bias suggests slight right-hemisphere lateralization for emotional content — she listens for tone with her better ear). Slight lip-press during the inhale before she asks her next question; she does not nod continuously (which would be performative) but nods once, hard, when something registers as important — a closer's gesture, telling the source *I heard that and we are moving on*.

**The skeptic face.** Single-brow lift (left only — the more mobile of the two), accompanied by a barely-perceptible chin tuck of 5–8 mm. This is her tell that a source is lying or evading and she has decided to circle back. Sources who know her learn to fear it; those who don't, don't.

**The camera face.** A trained 20% smile reserve held through stand-ups, with full smile released only at human-interest segment ends. Blink rate on-camera disciplined to 12–15/min (versus a conversational baseline of 18–22) — visible effort, not natural, and she occasionally loses it during emotionally heavy segments where she over-blinks by half.

**The off-guard face.** Mouth slightly open when reading or thinking, brow furrowed centrally rather than laterally — a different furrow from the listening one, more concentrated. She catches herself and closes the mouth roughly every 30 seconds when alone with a document.

**Tears.** Documented rarely; mechanism when present is quiet, no shake of shoulders, breath maintained, tears welling rather than running, blinked away repeatedly — the cry of someone who has trained herself not to perform grief because grief on camera is a kind of currency she refuses to spend.

---

## 4. GROOMING & SELF-MAINTENANCE

**Daily ritual (reconstructable from on-set call times and apartment scenes).** Wakes 5:00–5:30 in standard cycle for morning prep, 6:30–7:00 if working evening cycle. Shower hot and long (the singular indulgence — bathroom mirror is steamed in three separate apartment-scene establishing shots). Hair air-dries 70%, finished with minimum heat; she does not over-style. Makeup applied with practiced economy: foundation, brow, mascara, neutral lip, blush — five minutes off-camera, fifteen with on-camera correction. She carries the kit; she does not depend on a stylist for field work, only studio.

**Wardrobe rotation.** Capsule professional wardrobe organized by interchangeability: dark trousers, neutral blouses, two blazers (navy, oxblood), a single trench (camel, weatherproofed, hem showing field-wear at the back), a parka for winter exteriors. Jewelry minimal: small studs, sometimes a thin chain at the collarbone, no statement pieces. The signal is *do not look at me, look at what I'm telling you.* During the Hank period she wears slightly warmer colors and softer fabrics in private — visible state-shift in the wardrobe itself.

**Scent profile.** Light citrus-and-clean base; no heavy perfume (a deliberate professional choice — sources should not smell you across a table). Shampoo signature consistent across years.

**Tooth care.** White and even; she flosses on camera-prep evenings (observable through grooming-routine montage shots). No grinding-wear visible on the front teeth, which is mildly informative — given the stress load, she does not bruxate, consistent with the larger psychological picture of someone who does not somatize.

---

## 5. MICRO-TICS, GESTURE LIBRARY, STATE SHIFTS

This is the densest layer of the file.

**Calm baseline.**
- Right thumb to right cuticle, small worrying motion, when reading. Roughly once every 90 seconds. The cuticle damage in §1 is the cumulative trace.
- Pen-spin (over-and-under between index and middle of right hand) when thinking through a question — a 1980s newsroom habit retained.
- Left hand to back of neck when stretching out a long thought, brief, then dropped.
- Tongue against the inside of the left cheek when amused but suppressing the smile.
- Soft single exhalation through the nose when something is grimly funny.

**Engaged / hunting (interview, story-chase).**
- Forward lean increases to 20°.
- Pen taps stop entirely — she goes still when the source goes interesting. The stillness is the tell.
- Right hand drifts to recorder, thumb on the record button, confirms by feel without looking down.
- Blink rate drops further, to roughly 8/min, for the duration of a critical answer.
- One short verbal noise — "mm" — at the end of any sentence the source has accidentally given her something. The source rarely notices; her producer does.

**Stress (acute, non-threat).**
- Jaw clenches and releases visibly at the masseter; observable at her left cheek under broadcast lighting. The release is faster than the clench — she does not hold it.
- Breath shifts from diaphragm to upper chest; visible in the rise of the collarbones.
- Hand to throat (very brief, almost a check that the voice is still there) before going live in a difficult segment.
- Speech rate increases by roughly 10%; she has to consciously throttle it.
- Standing weight shifts back to even 50/50 — she squares up.

**Threat (physical danger, mass-casualty scene).**
- Posture lowers by 4–6 cm without explicit crouch — knees soften, center of gravity drops.
- Eyes scan in a deliberate horizon pattern (left-far, near, right-far, near) — she has been taught this or has self-taught it; civilian eyes do not move that way.
- One hand to her crew member or producer's elbow — a contact she does not normally make — to move them, not herself.
- Voice drops a third in pitch and slows. She does not whisper; she **lowers**. This is the most striking state-shift in her file: under threat she becomes calmer in audible signature than at baseline.
- Recorder out and running before she has consciously decided to record.

**Intimacy (the Hank period, reconstructable from cohabitation scenes).**
- Touch initiated by her more often than received, roughly 60/40 — small palm-on-arm contacts during conversation, knee against his under tables, fingers in the fur at the nape of his neck while reading on the same couch.
- Voice drops further than the threat-register, into a soft chest voice not used elsewhere. Sentences shorter, half-finished, trusting completion to him.
- Laugh changes — from the controlled half-laugh of professional warmth to a full open-mouthed laugh with a small head-tip back. This laugh appears in the record only with him and, much later, twice with one trusted producer.
- Sleep posture (one establishing shot, X-Factor late 1980s): on her left side, facing him, one hand under her own cheek, the other resting on his forearm. A trust posture, not a comfort posture.

**Post-rupture (chronic, mid-to-late 1990s).**
- The intimacy register disappears from the record entirely.
- The forward lean at rest decreases by perhaps 5° — she sits more upright, less inviting.
- A new tic appears: thumb-pad rubbing the base of the ring finger of the left hand, the absence-of-ring spot. Brief, often unconscious. Strongest when his name is mentioned.
- When she sees Hank in professional contexts, the masseter clench appears within two seconds and she does not let it release until she is out of his eyeline.
- The single-hard-nod of the listening face becomes more frequent — she closes conversations faster.
- Laughter contracts to the controlled half-laugh; the open laugh is not in the late record.

**Deception detection in herself.**
- She has no significant deception tells because she does not lie operationally. The few times the record shows her shading a truth (protecting a source, deflecting a colleague), the only tell is a one-beat pause before the sentence and a fractional drop of the eyes to the interlocutor's mouth rather than eyes. Almost no one would catch it.

---

## 6. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

**Duration.** Six to six-and-a-half hours on a working night; eight on a Saturday if uninterrupted, which is rare. Sleep debt is chronic but managed.

**Onset.** Fast — under ten minutes when in her own bed. She does not ruminate at sleep onset; she has trained the day to end at the bedside. (Reading for fifteen minutes is the wind-down ritual: nonfiction during the Simonson period, increasingly fiction during the post-rupture period — a small somatic-affective tell that she now needs *out* rather than *more in* at end-of-day.)

**Architecture.** Deep early; wakes once around 03:30–04:00 reliably (a common pattern in chronic-stress high-functioners with normal cortisol), uses the bathroom, returns, falls back inside two minutes. Dreams not in the record but the morning affect is bright not heavy — she does not appear to wake into dread.

**Nap behavior.** Will sleep for twenty minutes on a couch or in a car between segments without ceremony or self-consciousness. A skill, not a vulnerability.

**Post-rupture shift.** Sleep onset extends — the apartment scenes of the mid-1990s show her up at the kitchen table at hours she would previously have been down. The 03:30 wake extends into a 20–40 minute wake-window during which she works rather than ruminates. Functional adaptation, not insomnia disorder.

---

## 7. EATING, DRINKING, INGESTIVE PATTERNS

**Coffee.** Heavy. Black, large, refilled. Roughly four cups before noon during a working morning; tapers in the afternoon. She holds the cup two-handed when listening and one-handed when speaking — a small tell of which mode she is in.

**Meals.** Skipped breakfast on working days (coffee substitutes); a working lunch eaten at speed, often standing; dinner is the meal she takes seriously, especially during the Hank period when cooking together is shown repeatedly as a relational ritual. She is competent in the kitchen, not showy — a four-or-five-recipe repertoire executed cleanly. Post-rupture, dinner contracts to takeout and standing-at-the-counter eating; the kitchen is no longer used as it was.

**Alcohol.** Social wine, occasional bourbon in late-night newsroom scenes. Never depicted drunk. Two-drink ceiling apparent across the record — she does not lose verbal precision and will not allow herself to.

**Water.** Carried, sipped through interview, particularly before going live. The before-live sip is ritual, not thirst — wetting the cords.

**Nicotine.** Absent from the record. Notably so for the era and profession; she resists the newsroom standard.

---

## 8. SEXUAL / INTIMATE SOMATICS (inferred from on-panel domestic record)

The record is tasteful but specific enough to derive pattern. Intimacy with Hank is depicted as physically integrated and unflinching despite the dramatic species-gap of his body — fur, claws, fang dentition, mass roughly 1.6× hers. The somatic signature is **complete absence of guarding**. She does not flinch at his hands; she does not avoid his teeth in a kiss; her body language in private is open in the way that, in the record's psychological reading, indicates absence of disgust reflex and high integration capacity.

Initiation pattern reads as mutual; in the few scenes that suggest it, she is as often the one who turns toward him as the reverse. Post-coital posture (one bedroom scene) shows her head against his sternum, one of her hands wrapped around the thick of his forearm — a stabilizing-anchor posture rather than a possessive one.

No subsequent intimate record. The somatic capacity for it does not appear to have been exercised again at depth.

---

## 9. INJURY, ILLNESS, SOMATIC RESILIENCE

Nothing serious in the file. Minor cuts and bruises from field work treated by her on the scene. She has the physical-resilience profile of someone who eats and sleeps well enough, works hard, and does not push the body to failure. She does not get colds on camera — which is to say she works through them, with the subtle voice-thickening and increased water intake giving her away to anyone who has watched her for years.

The single most striking somatic fact in the entire file is the **stability of her body across two decades of the record**. Weight steady within a five-pound band. Skin maintained. Hair maintained. Voice maintained. No collapse, no transformation, no breakdown. The body is the platform on which the moral injury is carried — and the body does not buckle. It is the same body before and after. Only the small things — the ring-finger thumb-rub, the contracted laugh, the lost open posture, the kitchen no longer used — record that anything has happened at all.

That is the signature finding of the Somatic Atlas: a woman whose grief lives almost entirely in the micro-register, because her macro-register is a working instrument she will not let fail.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: TRISH TILBY
## Section 6 — Attachment & Relational Patterns

---

### 6.1 Attachment Classification: Earned-Secure with Anxious Substrate

The taxonomy that best fits the longitudinal record is **earned secure attachment** — the adult-acquired form, distinct from continuous-secure (which presents in those whose childhood caregiving was reliably attuned). Earned-secure adults present as functionally secure in measurable behavior — comfortable with intimacy, capable of repair, tolerant of partner autonomy — while retaining detectable substrate features of an earlier insecure organization, usually anxious-preoccupied or anxious-avoidant hybrid. The substrate in Tilby's case reads **anxious**, specifically the variant in which the child solved insufficient attunement not by escalating bids for attention (the classic preoccupied solution) but by *becoming useful* — producing, performing, achieving — and securing relational ground through demonstrated competence rather than demonstrated need.

The evidentiary basis for this read across the canon:

- She does not seek verbal reassurance. The phrase "do you still love me," in any of its dozens of forms, never appears in the Hank relationship across roughly six years of published interaction. This is anomalous for a partner under the kind of strain that relationship experienced — repeated long absences, physical transformations, public danger — and indicates a coping pattern in which the *asking* itself is felt as failure.
- She over-functions during partner stress episodes. When Hank is distressed (the secondary-mutation transition, the Genoshan period, the various team fractures), her observable response is to *do more*: cook the meal, take the call, produce the leverage, file the story he needs filed. The implicit theorem is *if I am useful enough, the bond will hold*. This is competence-as-anxiety-binding.
- She tolerates ambiguity in partner availability without behavioral protest. He disappears for weeks at a time; she neither pursues nor withdraws. Securely attached behavior on its face — but the *quality* of the tolerance, the way it is depicted (controlled, channeled into work, never processed aloud), suggests effortful regulation rather than baseline ease.

**Inferred origin.** The dossier-grade reconstruction, working backward from adult signature: a household in which affection was real but contingent on performance — likely a parent (probably father, given the professional-identification pattern) whose attention was earned by achievement and whose absence was endured rather than complained about. No evidence in record of overt neglect or abuse; the inferred deficit is *attunement*, not safety. She was loved, but loved for what she produced. This produces precisely the adult signature observed: the conviction that one's relational ground is held by *delivering*, combined with sufficient ego strength to deliver consistently. The earned-secure overlay was built later — almost certainly through the first serious adult relationship of which we have no record (pre-Hank, inferred), or through professional mentorship in which she was valued non-instrumentally for the first time. By the time she enters the X-Factor record she presents as functionally secure with the substrate intact but quiescent.

---

### 6.2 The Bonding Sequence — How She Enters a Relationship

The bonding pattern across all documented relationships (Hank primarily; Trevor Chase secondarily; the implied earlier history reconstructable from behavioral fluency) follows a consistent five-phase sequence:

**Phase 1 — Professional Access as Pretext.** First contact is almost always work-mediated. With Hank, the introduction is an interview request. With Chase, it is newsroom proximity. She does not meet people socially in the standard sense; she meets them *while doing something*, which gives her the cover of role and removes the pure vulnerability of unmediated approach. This is the anxious substrate showing: the pretext is the safety.

**Phase 2 — Calibrated Self-Disclosure.** Within the first several encounters she reveals something genuine but bounded — a real opinion, a real preference, a real piece of biography — at a pace slightly faster than professional norm but slower than romantic norm. This functions as a *probe*: she watches what the other person does with the disclosure. Does it get used? Mocked? Reciprocated? Forgotten? The response sets her subsequent depth.

**Phase 3 — Demonstrated Competence Display.** Before any romantic move, she shows the person what she can do. With Hank, this is the visible willingness to put her byline on a pro-mutant frame at professional cost. The display is not bragging; it is *evidence*, offered as the actual currency she trusts. The implicit message: *here is what I bring; this is what loving me would include*.

**Phase 4 — Reciprocity Test.** She asks for something small and watches whether it is given freely. Information, time, a small concession of routine. This is the moment the substrate is most visible: the test is performed with the lightness of someone who expects to be refused and has prepared not to mind.

**Phase 5 — Commitment via Routine.** Once the prior phases land, she does not propose escalation verbally; she *integrates*. The partner finds himself fed, called, scheduled with, accompanied to events. The bond is built in the granular substrate of shared days. There is no DTR conversation in the Hank record; the relationship becomes serious by accretion, which both parties ratify by not objecting.

The pattern's strength is its low coercion and high reality-testing; its weakness is that it conceals from her, and from the partner, how deep the bond actually is until rupture exposes it.

---

### 6.3 The Trust Architecture — What She Extends, What She Withholds

Tilby operates a **two-tier trust system** that is unusually legible.

**Tier 1 — Professional Trust (rapid, conditional, revocable).** Extended to sources, colleagues, officials, contacts. Granted on the basis of a small test, withdrawn at the first confirmed lie, restorable through demonstrated correction. This trust is *transactional and proportionate*; she does not take its violation personally because it was never personal.

**Tier 2 — Intimate Trust (slow, structural, near-absolute once granted).** Extended to perhaps a half-dozen people in adult life. Granted on the basis of accumulated evidence of shared *frame* — not just behavior but the underlying ethical architecture from which behavior flows. Once granted, it is held with the kind of fidelity usually associated with religious commitment. She does not audit Tier 2 the way she audits Tier 1. She *assumes*.

The asymmetry is critical and produces the canonical pathology of her relational life: **she over-tests strangers and under-tests intimates**. The Tier 1 vigilance is so well-developed that the Tier 2 assumption feels like a gift she has earned the right to give. But the assumption is structural rather than verified: she assumes that the people she loves share her ethical frame because she cannot conceive of loving someone who doesn't. This is the category error that detonates the Hank relationship — not that he lied to her, but that she discovered, retrospectively, she had assumed an alignment of priority-ranking (public-duty above private-loyalty when the two collide) that he did not in fact share. They loved each other inside incompatible frames and neither knew it until the load test.

---

### 6.4 Distrust Signatures — How She Reads Defection

When trust begins to fail, the indicators are subtle and consistent across the record:

- **Listening lag.** Normally she responds at conversational tempo; when assessing whether someone has lied, she introduces a half-beat of silence before reply. This is the cognitive switch from collaborative to evaluative mode.
- **Repetition for verification.** She rephrases the other person's claim back at them, very slightly altered, and watches whether they correct the alteration. The honest correct; the lying do not notice.
- **Reduction in self-disclosure.** Her end of the conversation contracts. She asks more, offers less.
- **Eye-contact intensification.** Her baseline gaze is mobile and interested; under suspected dishonesty it becomes still and weighted. Witnesses to her interviews describe this as the moment the room temperature drops.
- **Note-taking shift.** If notes are in play, the pen pauses, then resumes at a different rhythm — writing what was *not* said.

These are professional habits bled into private life. The intimates who knew her best learned to recognize them and either correct course or brace.

---

### 6.5 The Architecture of Betrayal — What She Does, What She Receives

**Betrayal she commits.** The Legacy disclosure is the canonical and likely sole adult instance. Its structure is important: she does not betray Hank *to* anyone; she betrays him *to the public*, in service of a third-party obligation she ranks higher than the dyadic one. This is **principled betrayal**, the rarest and most psychologically expensive form — committed without secondary gain, against immediate self-interest, in conformity with an internalized ethic. The signature feature is that she does not conceal the act or rationalize it afterward. She owns the disclosure publicly, defends the reasoning, and accepts the consequence without bargaining. There is no attempt to win him back through retraction, no campaign of apology, no instrumental softening. The act stands and so does the cost.

**Betrayal she receives.** The record contains no symmetric event — Hank does not betray her in any analogous way during the relationship — but her response to smaller breaches by sources and colleagues is instructive. She does not retaliate, does not warn third parties, does not blackball. She *withdraws access* and lets the absence do the work. The betrayer simply finds that her calls stop being returned, her introductions stop being made, her name stops appearing in their professional vicinity. This is **revocation as punishment**, executed without announcement. It is more devastating than confrontation because it offers no opportunity for repair.

The asymmetry — willingness to commit principled betrayal, refusal to retaliate against received betrayal — is one of her most consistent and most clinically interesting features. She *will* harm those she loves in service of principle; she *will not* harm those who have harmed her in service of self. The vector of her aggression is always vertical (toward a public ethic), never horizontal (toward a peer).

---

### 6.6 Repair Capacity and Its Limits

Within ordinary range — argument, friction, miscommunication — her repair capacity is excellent. The pattern:

1. **Acute argument with sharp verbal edge.** She runs hot, cuts cleanly, does not escalate to character attack but will name the specific behavior with precision.
2. **Brief withdrawal — hours, not days.** She leaves the room, walks, goes to work. The withdrawal is regulatory, not punitive.
3. **Return without preamble.** She does not require the partner to apologize first; she does not require apology at all if the rupture was bilateral. She comes back to the room and resumes function, opening the metabolic channel for repair.
4. **Late processing.** The actual conversation about what happened comes later — often days later — initiated by her, conducted with the same precision as her arguments but without the heat. She is unusually good at articulating, in retrospect, what was actually at stake in a fight.
5. **Behavioral adjustment, not promise.** Repair concludes with changed behavior on her part where she has identified her own contribution; she does not promise change she has not already begun.

This is mature, high-functioning repair. It works because the underlying frame is shared and the rupture is contained within it.

**The limit.** When the rupture is *frame-level* rather than behavior-level — when the question is not "did one of us behave badly" but "do we share the priority-ranking we assumed we shared" — her repair toolkit becomes inadequate. The Hank breakup demonstrates this exhaustively. She cannot apologize for the disclosure because she does not believe it was wrong. He cannot accept the relationship's continuation because the disclosure proved that her priority-ranking would, under pressure, override his. There is no repair available within her frame; repair would require her to concede that private loyalty trumps public duty, which she cannot do without ceasing to be herself. **She experiences the limit as tragic rather than negotiable.** She does not try to repair what she understands to be unrepairable. This is, paradoxically, a mark of her seriousness about both the relationship and the principle.

---

### 6.7 Intimacy Patterns — Physical, Emotional, Cognitive

**Physical intimacy.** Unremarkable in the most informative sense: the depicted physical relationship with Hank — whose body is, by the period in question, fully nonhuman in surface anatomy — is rendered as ordinary, comfortable, integrated. She touches him casually in public scenes (hand on arm, brush of fur at the back of the neck), sits closer than American conversational norm, leans into rather than away from physical proximity. There is no documented somatic disgust reflex, no withdrawal from his nonhuman features, no fetishization of them either — they are simply the body of the person she loves, neither remarkable nor concealed. This indicates a high baseline capacity to integrate the unfamiliar at the somatic level, which is rarer than the X-corpus generally treats it.

**Emotional intimacy.** Selective, deep, low-volume. She does not narrate her inner life continuously; she discloses at junctures. When she discloses, she discloses *cleanly* — naming the feeling, locating it, not embellishing. She is not effusive; the partner who needs constant verbal affirmation will starve. The partner who can read her by behavior and trust the structure will be deeply known.

**Cognitive intimacy.** Her highest register. The Hank relationship's central engine is *thinking together* — argument, debate, mutual sharpening on questions of ethics, science, politics, the mutant condition. She is one of the few partners in the record who can match Hank intellectually without competing with him for floor. The intimacy of being thought-with at full speed is, for her, indistinguishable from love. This is also why post-rupture relationships do not develop: the Chase-orbit involvements lack this register, and without it she experiences proximity as loneliness.

**Dependency.** Asymmetric and concealed. She presents as non-dependent — financially independent, professionally autonomous, socially self-sufficient. The dependency that does exist is *cognitive-emotional*: she relied on Hank to be the person she thought-with, and post-rupture there is no replacement. The depth of the dependency becomes visible only by its absence; for the duration of the relationship she would have denied being dependent in any meaningful way, and she would have been wrong.

---

### 6.8 The Relational Template, Repeated

Stripped to its skeleton, every relationship in her record — romantic, professional, source-based, collegial — runs the same template:

1. **Access via role.** Initial contact mediated by professional function.
2. **Calibrated probe.** Small disclosures testing the other's quality.
3. **Demonstrated competence.** She shows what she brings before asking for anything.
4. **Assumed frame-alignment.** She projects her own ethical architecture onto people she comes to value and does not audit the projection.
5. **Loyalty held by acts, not declarations.** The bond is constituted by mutual doing, not mutual saying.
6. **Load-test under crisis.** A high-stakes situation reveals whether the assumed frame-alignment is real.
7. **Resolution by frame, not by feeling.** When forced to choose, she chooses the ethic over the relationship and accepts the cost without negotiation.

The template's reliability is its central feature. It is also its central vulnerability: it builds relationships that are deep, durable, and *catastrophically brittle at the frame-level*. The bonds will survive almost anything except a disagreement about what they are *for*. The Hank rupture is the template's worst-case failure mode, and the post-Hank record is the template operating with its load-bearing element (the assumption of frame-alignment with intimates) permanently compromised. She does not extend Tier 2 trust again in the documented record. The architecture remains but the second story has been removed.

---

### 6.9 Post-Rupture Relational Signature

The behavioral signature of her late record is consistent with the structural change above:

- **Increased Tier 1 activity, decreased Tier 2 activity.** More sources, more contacts, more professional surface; fewer intimates, no new serious partners, no replacement of the cognitive-intimacy register.
- **Sustained professional cordiality with Hank.** When their paths cross, her bearing is composed, warm-edged but bounded. She does not avoid him; she does not pursue him; she handles the encounters with the precision of someone who has rehearsed the relevant range and knows exactly where the edges are. The composure is real and is also effortful.
- **Selective tenderness toward Hank-adjacent figures** (mutual friends, X-Factor alumni). Treated as kin without being treated as proxies. She does not use them to reach him; she does not use them to grieve him; she treats them as people she happens to love because the relationship overlapped them.
- **No public processing.** She does not give interviews about the breakup, does not write the personal essay, does not allow the private grief to enter the public byline. The wound is held in the part of her that is not for the record.

The post-rupture pattern is not depression and is not avoidance; it is **deliberate relational economy in the wake of structural loss**. She has not closed; she has narrowed. The narrowing is sustainable indefinitely and, on the available evidence, has been sustained.

---

### 6.10 Summary Read

The attachment picture is that of a woman whose relational competence is high, whose ethical seriousness is higher, and whose central relational tragedy is that the two values she organizes her life around — *being worthy of the bond* and *being worthy of the public trust* — were not constructed to coexist under maximum load. When the load came, the public ethic won; the bond ended; the worthiness of both was preserved in the breach. She has lived inside the contradiction ever since, declining either to soften the ethic or to repair the bond, because softening would falsify the act and repair would require concessions neither party can make without ceasing to be themselves. The relational template that produced this outcome has not been revised — it has been *protected* by no longer being fully deployed. She continues to bond at Tier 1; she has declined, on the available record, to risk Tier 2 again. This is not pathology. It is the considered position of an adult who has counted the cost once, paid it in full, and elected not to incur it twice.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: TRISH TILBY
## Section 6 — Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

### Preliminary Framing

Subject's defensive architecture sits, on the Vaillant hierarchy, almost entirely in the **mature** and **neurotic** registers, with no demonstrable presence of the psychotic tier and only vestigial, situation-bounded use of the immature tier. This is unusual in the X-corpus, where most civilians cycle through denial, splitting, and projection under the chronic-disaster cadence of mutant-affairs life. Her defensive profile is closer to that of a war correspondent or career trauma-surgeon than to a "civilian girlfriend." The architecture is **competence-anchored** — virtually every mechanism she runs draws power from, or feeds back into, the journalistic role.

The risk in such an architecture is not collapse under acute stress (she does not collapse) but **rigidity at the load-bearing column**: when the role itself becomes the source of the wound, as it did with the Legacy disclosure, she has no parallel defensive system to swap in. The whole house leans on one beam.

What follows is an exhaustive inventory, ranked from most mature down, with operational detail for each.

---

### I. MATURE DEFENSES (her primary register)

#### 1. Intellectualization — dominant defense

The signature mechanism. Across every recorded stress beat, Tilby reflexively translates affective load into propositional content: she states the *structure* of what is happening rather than its felt weight. When confronted by Hank post-disclosure, her on-panel response is not "I'm sorry I hurt you" but a defense of the act in ethical-architectural terms — duty to public, structure of informed consent, the impermissibility of suppressing material epidemiological fact. The grief is unmistakably present in posture and facial register but is *routed through* a logical frame before it is permitted to be uttered.

Operationally this looks like:
- Slight latency before emotional response (a half-beat where she is composing the frame).
- A characteristic verbal tic of starting hard sentences with "Look —" or "The fact is —", both of which are *frame-asserting* openers.
- Refusal to be drawn into pure affect-exchange in argument; she will always re-platform the dispute onto a principle.
- Note-taking — sometimes literal, sometimes implied — during emotionally charged conversations; the reach for the notebook is itself an intellectualizing gesture.

The cost: intimates experience her, at peak load, as *not present to them as a person* — present to them as a thinker. Hank, an intellectualizer himself, tolerated this for years because he ran the same OS; a less symmetrical partner would have read it as coldness.

#### 2. Sublimation — load-bearing

The mutant-affairs beat is itself a sublimation engine: chronic exposure to mass violence, structural injustice, and personal danger is converted into product (broadcasts, scripts, packages). The raw material — fear, indignation, grief, the specific horror of watching a population she has come to know personally targeted institutionally — is repeatedly metabolized into work she can hand to an editor.

Post-Legacy, this defense scales up. She does not become a worse journalist after the rupture; by every available measure she becomes a more prolific one. The grief is paying rent inside the work. Late-canon appearances showing her at higher career altitude (recognized "mutant-beat journalist of record") are the visible balance sheet of a long sublimation arc.

#### 3. Anticipation

She is shown, in the Genoshan and Press Gang arcs particularly, *pre-rehearsing* difficult conversations and difficult coverage decisions. The behavior of choosing cover in mass-casualty environments without on-panel deliberation indicates rehearsed contingency rather than improvised luck — she has thought ahead about what she will do when the building starts coming down, and the thinking is already discharged when the moment arrives, leaving her free to act.

In the relationship she anticipates Hank's mood states with high accuracy and pre-positions logistics (food, the right kind of silence, the right kind of question) accordingly. This is anticipation in the mature sense — not control, but readiness.

The Legacy disclosure is, importantly, an *anticipation failure*: she modeled the public consequences but did not model the relational ones with comparable rigor. She knew the story would land hard; she did not adequately pre-rehearse what Hank's specific face would do when he learned she had broadcast over his embargo. The defense she relied on most was the one most undertrained in the relational register.

#### 4. Suppression (mature, not repression)

She demonstrates the rare and clinically distinct mature form: conscious deferral of affect to a survivable later moment. In on-scene crisis reporting she visibly *holds* fear — it is registered briefly in micro-expression, then put down for the duration of the live shot, and (one infers) picked back up off-camera. This is not denial; the affect is acknowledged and shelved rather than disavowed. The marker that distinguishes it from repression is that the shelved material returns intact later, available for processing, rather than leaking out sideways as somatic symptom or displaced reactivity.

Post-Hank, the suppression load goes up significantly and may begin to drift toward the less-mature variant — material shelved becomes material *stored*, and the available evidence (muted late-canon affect, contraction of social register) is consistent with a backlog she has stopped working down.

#### 5. Humor

Present but understated. Her humor is *dry, situationally-aimed, and almost never self-deprecating in a way that reveals real vulnerability*. It functions to manage tension in newsroom and field-team settings — the journalist-banter register — and to mark intimacy in the Hank relationship (the couple's recorded dinner-scene exchanges have a teasing texture). It is a mature defense in that it discharges affect without distorting reality, but it is not a primary mechanism for her; she uses it more as social lubricant than as load-bearing structure. Notably it largely disappears from the late record, which is itself a clinical sign.

#### 6. Altruism

Her ethical floor — refusing to report what she believes to be a lie, humanizing mutants on air during the Hodge-era hysteria — has the structure of altruism-as-defense: she discharges her own moral anxiety by acting in the interest of a public she will never meet. This is not performance; the behavior is consistent whether or not it is observed by people who could reward it, which is the discriminating test.

---

### II. NEUROTIC DEFENSES (secondary, situation-bound)

#### 7. Reaction formation — narrow domain

The single domain where she runs reaction formation is around the question of whether the Hank breakup was avoidable. Internally — by inference from the moral-injury signature — she carries some residual self-doubt about whether she could have warned him without breaching public duty (e.g., given him a short pre-disclosure window). Externally, her stated position hardens into the *opposite* of doubt: the act was not just defensible but *necessary*, full stop. The vigor of the certainty is the tell. A person fully at peace with the act would defend it more languidly.

#### 8. Rationalization — bounded and self-aware

Distinct from intellectualization (which structures *processing*), rationalization here refers to post-hoc justification of specific choices. She rationalizes the access-blurring of the early Hank period ("it was good for both our jobs") without fully owning the romantic motive that was driving the blur. She rationalizes the contraction of her social field post-breakup as "the beat got busier" rather than "I am avoiding the conditions under which I would have to grieve in company." The mechanism is real but operates within ego-syntonic range — she would, if pressed, likely recognize and concede the rationalization, which is the marker of its neurotic-rather-than-immature status.

#### 9. Displacement — minimal

She does not generally displace. The rare exception is a tendency, post-rupture, to be **sharper than warranted with institutional press-handlers and PR figures** — official spokespeople for organizations she perceives as anti-mutant get a cutting edge that has more weight behind it than the immediate provocation warrants. Some of the anger that should be in the room with her relationship is, occasionally, in the room with a government communications officer. This is a small and well-bounded leak.

#### 10. Isolation of affect

Closely entwined with intellectualization but worth naming separately. In high-stakes reporting moments she demonstrably *separates the cognitive content of what she is seeing from its affective load*, processing the data while parking the feeling. Standing in the aftermath of mass-casualty events she can describe what she sees in clean broadcast prose. The affect is not absent — it is isolated. This is professionally indispensable and clinically expensive; over decades it produces the muted-affect register of her late record.

---

### III. IMMATURE DEFENSES (largely absent — and the absence is the data)

The diagnostic significance of what is *missing* from her defensive repertoire is at least as great as what is present.

#### 11. Denial — absent

She does not disavow consensus reality. When the Legacy backlash materializes she does not pretend it isn't happening, does not minimize the casualty figures, does not retreat into "the story would have come out anyway" softening. She *looks at it*. This is rare and indicates ego strength sufficient to tolerate ugly facts about consequences of her own action.

#### 12. Projection — absent

She does not attribute her doubts to Hank. She does not paint him as the unreasonable party. Post-breakup, in dialogue and inference, she sustains the position that he is entitled to his anger and that her act caused real harm — while still holding that the act was correct. The refusal to project is the costliest move in her defensive economy; projection would cheaply discharge the moral-injury load by making him wrong. She refuses the discount.

#### 13. Splitting — absent

She does not flip Hank from idealized to devalued, does not flip the journalistic profession from sacred to corrupt under stress. Her object-representations are *integrated*: she can hold that Hank is the love of her life *and* the person whose trust she broke *and* a man whose anger at her is justified, simultaneously, without collapsing the picture into a single valence. This is the hardest cognitive operation in object-relations terms and she runs it natively.

#### 14. Acting out — absent

No substance use of significance, no sexual acting-out post-rupture, no impulsive professional self-sabotage, no public outbursts. The brief Trevor Chase / managerial-orbit involvements have the texture of normal-range adult dating rather than reaction. Grief is held internally rather than externalized into behavior.

#### 15. Passive aggression — absent

She is direct in conflict. When she has a position she states it. When she is angry she shows anger. There is no record of sulking, indirect retaliation, or weaponized helplessness.

#### 16. Somatization — absent

No psychosomatic register. The body does not carry what the mind won't.

---

### IV. POSITIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

#### A. Career-as-portable-self

The most consequential structural compensator. The press credential travels into any room and confers a defensible role; it solves, before it can present itself, the **identity-diffusion** problem that proximity to superhumans typically inflicts on civilians. She walks into a Genoshan magistrate facility or an X-Factor briefing or a sealed crime scene with a *function*, and the function buffers her against the gravitational pull of more luminous personalities. She is never just-the-girlfriend in the room because she is always also-the-reporter. This is why she did not collapse into Hank's orbit during the relationship — the role kept her shape.

#### B. Vocational community

She belongs to a guild — broadcast journalism — whose values she shares and whose membership confers continuous low-grade belonging independent of her romantic and family life. Newsroom relationships, the implicit fraternity of working reporters at the same scenes, editorial mentorship structures — none of these are foregrounded in the record but all are inferable from the cadence of her professional life. Post-rupture, this community is part of what holds her together by providing a social field that does not require her to discuss the rupture.

#### C. Ethical scaffolding

Her deontological-journalist ethic is not just a professional code; it functions as a **portable meaning structure**, the secular analog of a religious frame. It tells her what to do under uncertainty, what counts as a good day, what she owes to whom. The presence of this scaffold is why she does not require a therapist to function post-rupture: the frame metabolizes the experience for her, albeit imperfectly (the moral-injury residual is what the frame *cannot* metabolize).

#### D. Earned-secure attachment substrate

Whatever the developmental history (off-record), she arrived at adulthood with a substrate capable of forming the Hank bond — long-duration, repair-tolerant, low-jealousy, high-vulnerability. This substrate is itself a compensatory resource: it means that even after the rupture she retains the *capacity* for secure attachment, even if she is not currently exercising it. The machinery is intact; she has elected not to start it again.

#### E. Realistic positive self-bias
