Slightly above-realistic but not inflated self-concept. This is the empirically established correlate of resilience — people with mild positive bias recover from setbacks better than perfectly calibrated realists. She has enough of it to keep going and not enough to distort her assessments.

#### F. Capacity to tolerate cognitive dissonance

Possibly her single most distinctive psychological asset. She can hold "I did right" and "I caused harm" and "I lost what I loved" in the same internal room without forcing a resolution. Most adults force one of those propositions into subordination to relieve the pressure; she does not. This capacity is itself defensive — it prevents her from running the cheap escape routes (recantation, demonization of Hank, self-loathing) — but it costs her chronic low-grade psychic load.

---

### V. NEGATIVE / COSTLY COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

#### A. Over-identification with role

The mirror image of the portable-self benefit. Because the role does so much defensive work, the role becomes *non-negotiable*: she cannot let it lose, cannot subordinate it to a competing claim, even when the competing claim is the most important relationship of her life. Legacy disclosure is the moment the role's defensive utility shaded into defensive *rigidity* — the role had become so structurally load-bearing that to deprioritize it momentarily would have threatened the whole edifice. So she did not deprioritize it. So she lost Hank.

#### B. Work-as-affect-binding

Post-rupture acceleration of work intake is textbook use of vocation to absorb affect with nowhere else to go. The mechanism functions — she remains productive, remains sane — but the affect is bound, not processed. Over years this produces the muted register of late appearances: not depression, but a kind of low-amplitude flatness, the signature of a long-running emotional containment program.

#### C. Social-field contraction

Post-Hank, her depicted social world narrows. New deep relationships are not pursued. This is partly avoidance (the conditions under which she would have to grieve in company are conditions she is opting out of) and partly economy (the work is absorbing her bandwidth). The contraction is functional in the short term and erosive in the long term — fewer relationships means fewer opportunities for the spontaneous repair experiences that gradually heal moral-injury wounds.

#### D. Asymmetric anticipation

She anticipates professional and physical contingencies with high fidelity and *under-anticipates relational ones*. This asymmetry was visible pre-Legacy (the access-blurring of the early Hank period was relationally under-modeled) and was catastrophically visible at the disclosure itself. It is likely to recur if she ever does form another deep attachment — she will see the work risks coming and miss the relationship risks.

#### E. Frame-lock under pressure

Her acute-stress pattern of narrowing focus and resolving rather than deliberating is a real defensive asset in mass-casualty environments and a real defensive liability in relational ones. Once she has settled on a frame ("this is a public-health story, and public-health stories must be told"), she will not be argued out of it within the decision window. The defense saves her in collapsing buildings and damns her in collapsing relationships.

#### F. Refusal to discharge moral injury

The election to live in the contradiction rather than resolve it is, viewed defensively, a *negative* compensatory mechanism — she is using ego strength to *prevent* the cheap resolutions her psyche would otherwise reach for. This is admirable and is also the source of her unhealed-ness. Most people heal moral injuries by quietly recanting (over years, drift the conviction soft) or quietly demonizing the harmed party (over years, decide they had it coming) or quietly self-flagellating (over years, decide the conviction was always wrong). She is doing none of those, which means the wound is *not closing*. The refusal is principled; the cost is permanent low-grade grief.

---

### VI. Defensive Failure Modes (predictive)

Given the architecture above, the conditions under which her defenses are most likely to fail are:

1. **Public praise for the Legacy story from a figure she respects.** Forces collision between the conviction (defended by intellectualization and reaction formation) and the grief (held by suppression and isolation of affect). Likely produces brief, uncharacteristic affective breakthrough — visible tears, leaving the room, possibly a sharp word she regrets.

2. **Sudden re-encounter with Hank in an unstructured setting.** Structured professional re-encounters she has rehearsed (anticipation); an unrehearsed one — running into him at a gallery, a hospital, a private dinner — bypasses the prepared frame.

3. **Being asked to suppress a story that would harm someone she loves.** Recapitulates the original choice architecture; she will choose the same way and will know she is choosing the same way, which compounds rather than relieves the moral-injury load.

4. **Chronic professional stagnation.** If sublimation lost its outlet — being demoted, sidelined, or losing the mutant beat — the affective load currently bound in work would have nowhere to go and the architecture would begin to deform. This is the failure scenario most relevant to long-term welfare assessment.

5. **An intimate partner who refuses intellectualization as a mode of repair.** Anyone who insists she feel-first-justify-later will trigger her isolation-of-affect and intellectualization defenses simultaneously and will experience her as cold. She will not be able to retool the architecture to meet them in the time the encounter allows.

---

### VII. Summary

Trish Tilby runs a high, clean, mature defensive architecture supported by a stable vocational identity and an integrated object-relational substrate. The architecture is unusually free of the immature mechanisms (denial, projection, splitting, acting out) that would let her cheaply discharge the Legacy-disclosure wound; the refusal to use those mechanisms is itself a defensive choice with permanent cost. Her single architectural vulnerability is the over-loading of one beam — the journalistic role — which carries identity, meaning, social belonging, and affect-binding all simultaneously, and which therefore cannot be subordinated without structural risk. She knows this, on some level, and has organized her remaining life to ensure the beam is not asked to bear less than it currently bears. The grief is the rent.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: TRISH TILBY
## Section — Longitudinal Psychological Profile

A decade-by-decade clinical mapping. Where the published record is sparse, inference is flagged. The organizing claim: Subject's psychology is not static across the record but follows a **three-phase arc** — *ascending integration* (late 1980s) → *coupled equilibrium with latent fault line* (early 1990s) → *post-rupture consolidation around an unresolved moral wound* (mid-1990s onward). The frameworks used are standard: Vaillant's hierarchy of ego defenses, Bowlby/Main attachment categories, Linehan's affect-regulation model, Higgins's self-discrepancy theory, and the moral-injury construct as developed by Litz, Shay, and Maguen.

---

### Phase I — Late 1980s: The Ascending Reporter (approx. ages late-20s)

**Affect regulation.** Baseline arousal is elevated and *task-bound*. The earliest appearances (Simonson-era X-Factor, Mutant Hysteria coverage) show her in a state of sustained mobilization — leaning into shots, microphone-forward posture, rapid speech cadence, minimal latency between question and follow-up. Clinically this maps to what Porges would call a high-ventral-vagal engagement state: socially online, physiologically alert, neither sympathetic-flooded nor collapsed. She does not display startle responses appropriate to her exposure level (mutant combat at close range), which indicates either (a) habituation already in progress from prior beats unseen in record, or (b) a constitutional low-reactivity profile of the kind Kagan flagged in the "low-reactive" infant temperament category. The behavioral record supports (b) more than (a): she enters her first depicted mass-mutant scene already calibrated. There is no rookie-correspondent tremor.

Affect down-regulation in this phase is **achieved via cognitive engagement** — she metabolizes adrenaline by *narrating it*, literally turning arousal into copy. This is a healthy mechanism but a load-bearing one: it depends on the existence of an audience and a frame. Strip either, and her down-regulation tools shrink.

**Cognitive style.** Verbal-integrative, frame-first. In this phase she shows the journalist's signature **prosecutorial sequencing**: identify the moral/structural shape of the situation, then collect facts that test it. This is associative rather than purely deductive — she is willing to be wrong about the frame, but unwilling to operate without one. Her interview behavior in the early Hodge-era media-environment scenes shows that she listens for the **embedded premise** of an answer, not just its content. That is a high-order cognitive habit, not trainable past a certain ceiling; she has it natively.

Working memory load tolerance appears high — she tracks multiple sources, multiple storylines, and multiple field locations without visible decompensation. Attentional control favors *top-down* (goal-driven) over *bottom-up* (stimulus-driven); spectacular mutant events do not derail her question lines.

**Self-concept.** Coherent, slightly above accurate (in the healthy positive-illusion band Taylor and Brown identified). Her *actual self* and *ideal self* are close (Higgins): she is largely the reporter she wants to be, with the gap being trajectory rather than deficit — she expects to be better, bigger, more central, and is working toward it. *Ought self* is articulated through professional ethics rather than internalized parental voice; the record gives no family-of-origin material, but the *texture* of her ethical voice is collegial-professional, not familial. She talks like someone formed in newsrooms.

Identity is **role-anchored but not role-fused**. She is a journalist; she is not *only* a journalist. The distinction matters: role-anchored individuals can survive role-loss; role-fused individuals cannot. In Phase I she is unambiguously the former.

**Defense profile.** Predominantly mature (Vaillant Level IV): sublimation (channeling appetite-for-conflict into the beat), anticipation (she pre-positions for stories), suppression (she sets feelings aside for shifts and reclaims them later). Neurotic-level defenses appear under specific pressure — *intellectualization* especially, which in this phase is adaptive scaffolding rather than the rigid wall it becomes later.

---

### Phase II — Early 1990s: The Coupled Period (approx. ages early-30s)

**Affect regulation.** Broadens. The coupling with Hank introduces a second regulation channel — co-regulation in the Schore/Siegel sense. Domestic scenes (cooking, evening debriefs, the small-apartment beats Peter David specialized in) show her *down-shifting* in a way the earlier record does not contain. She is depicted at rest, which is itself a clinical datum: the capacity to enter parasympathetic dominance reliably in a chosen environment is the somatic correlate of secure-base function. Hank is the secure base; the apartment is the safe haven.

Anger regulation in this phase shows its mature form. She runs hot in argument — cutting word choice, dropped voice, pointed pauses — but is observed to **repair** (initiates reconnection within scene-time, references the rupture, acknowledges contribution). The Gottman repair-attempt literature would code this as high-functioning; the absence of contempt (eye-rolls, mockery, name-calling) is the strongest single positive marker.

Sadness regulation is the *least tested* dimension in this phase and therefore the **least developed**. She has had little reason to grieve on-panel. This is consequential: it means that when grief arrives in Phase III, she meets it with under-rehearsed tools.

**Cognitive style.** Largely stable from Phase I but with a measurable shift toward **integrative complexity** — she begins holding multiple value-systems in productive tension (journalistic, relational, mutant-political) rather than ranking them strictly. Suedfeld's integrative-complexity construct would score her notably high in this period. She is willing to say "I see why you want me to hold this story *and* I see why I cannot" without collapsing the tension prematurely.

But: this integrative capacity has a **ceiling under acute stress**. Under deadline, under existential stakes, the ranking re-asserts and the journalistic ethic returns to the top of the stack. The Phase II equilibrium is therefore *stable in normal weather, fragile in storm*. She does not know this about herself yet. Hank does not know it about her. Neither, presumably, do her producers.

**Self-concept.** Expanded along the relational axis. Phase I self-concept was "competent reporter on a hard beat." Phase II adds "the woman Hank loves" — and integrates it without subordinating the first. She does not become Hank's girlfriend in the diminutive newsroom sense; she becomes a woman whose life now has a person in it. The categorical separation is preserved. This is the **earned-secure attachment** signature: integration without fusion.

A subtle self-discrepancy enlarges in this phase, however. Her *ought self* — what her ethics demand of her — does not modify in response to the coupling. Hank's safety, Hank's preferences, Hank's professional vulnerabilities are weighted in the *actual* self's calculus (she does favors, blurs role boundaries, leverages access on the team's behalf) but not encoded in the *ought*. The ought stays a journalistic ought. This is the structural vulnerability that the Legacy event will exploit.

**Defenses.** Still mature-dominant. Sublimation deepens (the relationship metabolizes some of the appetite-for-intensity that previously fed only the beat). Humor appears more in record — Peter David's hand, but also consistent with someone whose anxiety has lowered enough to permit play. Intellectualization recedes into background function.

---

### Phase III — Mid-1990s: The Rupture and Its Year (approx. ages mid-30s)

**The Legacy disclosure event** is the inflection. Treated clinically, it is not a *decision* so much as a *crystallization* — the integrative complexity of Phase II collapses to the Phase I ranking under acute stakes, and she acts inside that collapsed frame within minutes. The behavioral signature is **decisive narrowing**: speech accelerates, social consultation drops to zero, motor sequence is direct (to studio, to anchor desk, to air). This is not impulsivity in the disinhibition sense; it is the rapid execution of a long-held priority order that had been *latent* during the coupled period.

**Affect regulation, immediate post-event (weeks to months).** First visible breakdown of the Phase II equilibrium. The record shows:

- Acute grief affect on rare panels (tears, voice-break) — *brief, contained, not displayed in professional contexts*. She compartmentalizes effectively. Linehan would note that her distress tolerance is high but her **emotion-mind/wise-mind oscillation** narrows: she is mostly in *reasonable mind* publicly, mostly in *emotion mind* privately, with the *wise mind* synthesis briefly unavailable.
- No depicted dysregulation outward: no shouting matches with colleagues, no public emotional displays, no substance escalation.
- Sleep disruption is implied (haggard rendering in some post-rupture appearances; the lighting cues are the artist's flag).

**Cognitive style, immediate post-event.** Returns to Phase I prosecutorial sequencing but now turned **on herself**. She runs the Legacy decision repeatedly through the ethical frame and the frame keeps returning the same answer (the disclosure was right). The frame cannot deliver absolution because absolution was never its function. She is using the wrong instrument for the wrong question and her cognitive style does not yet contain the move of *putting the instrument down*.

This is the cognitive shape of **moral injury** as Shay describes it: a person of intact ethical capacity is wounded precisely by the integrity of their ethics — the act was right, the loss is real, the conviction will not yield the comfort that recantation would supply, and the grief will not yield to the comfort that conviction would supply. The two systems run in parallel and the person lives in the seam.

**Self-concept, immediate post-event.** The relational sub-self contracts sharply. The professional self is preserved but no longer expansive — the *being-loved-by-Hank* dimension that quietly buttressed it is gone, and the professional self alone is asked to bear what two selves bore. It bears it, but visibly more thinly. Higgins's self-discrepancy framework would predict (and the record shows) **agitation-related affect** when actual-self meets ideal-self (she is not the integrated woman she expected to be at this age) and **dejection-related affect** when actual-self meets ought-self (she did what she ought, and ought delivered ash). The dejection cluster predominates.

**Defenses, immediate post-event.** Intellectualization returns to load-bearing status — the journalistic defense of the act is rehearsed, articulated, available on call. This is adaptive in the short term (it keeps her functional, keeps the wound from infecting work) and maladaptive in the long term (it prevents the metabolizing of grief through narrative integration in any other register). She does not move to immature defenses: no projection onto Hank, no splitting of him into villain, no acting out, no somatization beyond the implied sleep disruption. Ego strength holds.

---

### Phase IV — Late 1990s onward: Consolidation Around the Wound (approx. ages mid-to-late 30s and beyond)

**Affect regulation.** New steady-state, distinct from Phase I and Phase II. Arousal baseline is *slightly lower* than Phase I — the appetite-for-intensity has not vanished but has been chastened. Range of expressed affect narrows: she is less observably joyful, less observably enraged, less observably tender. The clinical term is **affective constriction**, and it is the signature of unresolved chronic grief in high-functioning adults. She is not flat (no anhedonic vegetative picture), but the dynamic range has compressed by perhaps a third.

Co-regulation channel is closed. The Trevor Chase/managerial dalliance(s) are unsustained; the record contains no replacement secure base. She regulates alone, through work, through the same Phase I cognitive-engagement mechanism — but now with less recovery time between activations, because there is no domestic parasympathetic anchor. This is the somatic profile that precedes burnout, though she does not depict burnout per se. She maintains.

**Cognitive style.** Stable verbal-integrative core; integrative complexity has *reduced* from the Phase II peak but remains above Phase I baseline. She is less willing to entertain frames that would require her to relitigate the Legacy decision; she is more willing to entertain frames that complicate the *cost* of journalistic ethics generally. She has, in effect, learned a meta-frame: the ethic was right and the ethic is expensive. This meta-frame is mature thinking, the kind Erikson would code as the leading edge of **generativity vs. stagnation** — except she has no apprentice in record, no mentee, no obvious channel through which to transmit what she has learned. The generativity drive is present but unconsummated.

**Self-concept.** Stabilizes at a *narrower but durable* configuration. She is the mutant-beat journalist of record. She is the woman who broke the Legacy story. She is no longer auditioning to be loved unconditionally; the project has been closed without resolution. Higgins discrepancies persist but no longer produce acute affect — they have become **chronic background tone** rather than acute episodic distress. This is the standard trajectory of unresolved grief converted to character: the wound stops bleeding and starts informing.

Self-esteem remains functionally intact. She does not believe herself a bad person. She believes herself a person who paid a price.

**Defenses.** Mature-dominant remains the picture, but with intellectualization now structurally embedded rather than situationally deployed — it has become a feature of her cognitive style rather than a tool she reaches for. The risk this creates is **decreased access to the grief itself**: the defense that protected the function has, over years, sealed over the wound's surface. She may no longer be able to reach the grief deliberately even when reaching it would be therapeutic. This is the long-term cost of unmetabolized moral injury well-defended against.

Reaction formation is *absent*. She does not become anti-mutant; she does not become anti-journalism; she does not become anti-Hank. The wound is held in its original shape.

---

### Cross-Phase Synthesis

**Affect regulation** evolved: *task-bound mobilization* (I) → *co-regulated equilibrium* (II) → *compartmentalized grief management* (III) → *constricted solo steady-state* (IV). The arc is from high range achieved through engagement, to high range supported by relationship, to narrowed range supported by work alone.

**Cognitive style** evolved: *prosecutorial frame-first* (I) → *integrative complexity* (II) → *recursive self-prosecution* (III) → *meta-framed stability with reduced flexibility* (IV). She got more sophisticated and then deliberately less sophisticated, in the way people do when sophistication has cost them something they cannot replace.

**Self-concept** evolved: *role-anchored ascending* (I) → *role-anchored plus relational* (II) → *role-anchored contracting* (III) → *role-anchored consolidated, narrower, durable* (IV). The role-anchor never breaks. This is why she survives intact.

**Defenses** evolved: *mature-dominant with adaptive intellectualization* (I) → *mature-dominant with intellectualization recessed* (II) → *mature-dominant with intellectualization reactivated* (III) → *mature-dominant with intellectualization structurally embedded* (IV). She never drops below the neurotic level. This is rare.

The longitudinal signature is of a woman whose **ego strength is the constant** and whose **range is the variable**. She does not break. She narrows. The narrowing is the cost of having not broken — and, read clinically, is what she has chosen instead of either of the two available exits (recantation, self-forgiveness). She lives in the seam because the seam is, for her, the truthful place. The psychology is, finally, an *ethic in somatic form*.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — TRISH TILBY

## Framing Note

A psychiatric workup on Subject is, paradoxically, an exercise in disciplined *exclusion*. The temptation in any total-surveillance file on a civilian embedded in the X-corpus is to over-pathologize — the proximity to mutant catastrophe, the broken signature relationship, the narrowing of late-life affect all invite a diagnostic label. The record does not support one. What it supports is something subtler and harder to name: a high-functioning adult organized around a single unresolved moral wound, with a constellation of subclinical features clustered around that wound, and an unusually clean differential against the major categories. This section works through the affirmative findings first, then performs the rule-outs with the granularity the file demands.

---

## 1. AFFIRMATIVE FINDINGS

### 1.1 Adjustment Disorder, Chronic, with Depressed Mood (DSM-5 309.0 / ICD-11 6B43) — RESOLVED-TO-RESIDUAL

**Onset:** Approximately one to three months following the Legacy Virus broadcast (X-Factor #100-era, c. 1994). Identifiable stressor: the termination of the McCoy relationship and the contemporaneous public backlash to her disclosure.

**Symptom presentation as inferred from behavioral record:**
- Reduction in depicted off-duty texture in subsequent appearances (no dinner scenes, no apartment scenes, no leisure scenes).
- Increase in on-duty visibility — appearances during this period are nearly exclusively at scenes of mutant-affairs reporting, suggesting either real workload increase or selective availability (i.e., she is *where work is* and otherwise unfindable).
- Affect on-camera tightens: less of the Simonson-era animation, more of a contained, composed broadcast register. This is not flatness; it is professional discipline tightening over a private contraction.
- No depicted sleep disturbance, no depicted appetite change, no anhedonia in the clinical sense — she still appears to take pleasure in good work.

**Course:** The acute adjustment phase appears to have run its expected six-to-twelve-month course. What remains in the late record is residual rather than active — a baseline downward shift in affective range and social engagement that has stabilized rather than progressed. By the late-1990s appearances, the picture is best described as **adjustment disorder, in partial remission, with persistent attenuation of social/relational functioning.**

**Why this is the correct diagnosis rather than Major Depressive Disorder:** Vegetative signs absent. Agency preserved. Vocational function preserved and arguably enhanced. The mood disturbance is *contextually tethered* — it triggers on Hank-adjacent stimuli and on praise for the Legacy story (see Pressure Points, Section 5 of prior synthesis) but does not generalize. This is the textbook differential.

### 1.2 Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.10 / ICD-11 6B42) — SUBCLINICAL FEATURES

The relationship loss meets none of the conventional bereavement criteria (no death), but the *structure* of her response maps onto prolonged grief better than onto ordinary romantic loss.

**Affirmative features present:**
- **Persistent yearning** — inferable from the consistent visible residual feeling in every depicted post-rupture encounter with Hank across multiple writers (a remarkable consistency given the writer drift problem).
- **Difficulty re-engaging in relationships** — the brief, undeveloped Trevor Chase-adjacent involvements suggest attempts that did not take. She is not avoidant; she is *unable to recommit at the depth she previously demonstrated capable of*.
- **Sense that part of oneself has died** — inferable from the narrowing of self-presentation. Pre-rupture Trish has hobbies, opinions about food, jokes about Hank's reading list. Post-rupture Trish is depicted almost exclusively in professional register.
- **Identity disruption** — partial. She has not lost her professional identity (it is in fact what carried her through), but the *partnered self* has not been rebuilt.

**Features absent:**
- The intensity does not impair functioning beyond the relational domain.
- No suicidal ideation in record.
- No avoidance of reminders — she continues to cover mutant affairs, which is the most reliable possible source of reminders.

**Diagnostic call:** Does not meet threshold. Documented as **subclinical prolonged-grief features, chronic**, etiologically continuous with the adjustment reaction.

### 1.3 Moral Injury — PRIMARY ORGANIZING FEATURE

Moral injury is not a DSM diagnosis; it is a clinical construct (Litz, Shay) describing the psychological sequelae of perpetrating, witnessing, or failing to prevent acts that transgress deeply held moral beliefs — *or*, in the Shay variant, the betrayal of "what's right" in a high-stakes context by someone with legitimate authority, *or by oneself*.

The Subject's case is the **self-as-agent** variant with an inverted moral valence: she committed an act she believes was *right*, which produced consequences she experiences as harm she caused. This is the rarer and more difficult-to-treat presentation, because the standard therapeutic move (reframe the act as defensible) is unavailable — she has already done it, exhaustively, and the reframe does not relieve the affect.

**Signature features in the record:**
- **Coexistence of moral conviction and grief without resolution.** She does not recant the disclosure. She does not forgive herself for its consequences. Both states are stably maintained.
- **No demonization of the injured party.** Hank is not recast as villain, as unfair, as overreactive. The record is remarkably free of the splitting one would expect in a defensive self-protective response.
- **No self-demonization either.** She does not present as self-flagellating, does not perform contrition, does not seek absolution.
- **Functional preservation with affective constriction in the wounded domain only.** Classic moral injury signature — work intact, public role intact, but the relational/intimate domain that was the site of the injury remains foreclosed.

**Etiology:** The Legacy disclosure created a structural double-bind that her cognitive style made inescapable. Her **moral-frame-first** processing identified the public's right to know as the dominant ethical claim; her deontological-journalist worldview made suppression categorically impermissible; her intellectualization-dominant defense structure prevented her from softening the consequences in retrospect through revisionist emotional reasoning. She is, in effect, *too cognitively honest to heal the standard way*.

### 1.4 Occupational Hyperengagement (Sub-Workaholism)

Not at the threshold of behavioral addiction (ICD-11 has no formal workaholism category; the closest analog is "Other Specified Disorders Due to Addictive Behaviours"). The picture does not meet criteria — she does not work compulsively to the exclusion of physical health, does not show withdrawal in enforced rest, does not appear to derive escalating reward requiring escalating engagement.

What she does show is **work-as-affect-binding-structure**: vocational engagement functioning to contain affect that has lost its previous relational outlet. This is subclinical and adaptive at the dose deployed. It becomes pathological only if the work itself were removed — at which point the bound affect would re-emerge with the cumulative pressure of years.

**Clinical note:** Subject is highly resilient *while employed in the mutant beat*. Job loss, beat reassignment, or forced retirement would be predicted to produce a delayed but significant depressive decompensation. This is a **structural vulnerability**, not a current disorder.

---

## 2. COMORBIDITY ANALYSIS

The presenting picture is unusual in that the affirmative findings are not independently comorbid — they are **etiologically continuous**, all radiating from the single 1994 event. This is diagnostically clean and clinically informative: there is no pre-existing substrate of mood, anxiety, or personality pathology onto which the moral injury was grafted. The Subject was a high-functioning, ego-strong adult who experienced a single catastrophic moral-relational event and has organized around it for the remainder of the record.

**No comorbid substance use disorder.** Social drinking only; no escalation post-rupture, which is itself notable — the substance-use pathway is the modal coping route for moral injury in occupational populations (journalists, combat veterans, first responders), and her non-use indicates either constitutional disinclination or active counter-investment in lucidity. Given her cognitive style, the latter is more probable: she will not anesthetize the wound because anesthetizing it would feel like a second betrayal — of the conviction that the disclosure was right and the cost was real.

**No comorbid anxiety disorder.** Despite the occupational profile (deadline-driven, public-facing, high-stakes beat) and despite the ample trauma exposure, there is no panic, no generalized anxiety presentation, no social anxiety. The "journalist's metabolism" baseline of alert-energized is constitutional, not anxious.

**No comorbid eating, sleep, or somatoform pathology** in record.

---

## 3. COURSE OVER TIME

**Pre-1988 (inferred baseline):** Premorbid functioning intact and high. Career trajectory ascending. No indication of prior psychiatric history.

**1988–1993 (relationship era):** High function across all domains. Affective range broad. Relational depth demonstrated. This is the period that establishes she is *capable* of the full range, which is what makes the later contraction diagnostically meaningful rather than merely characterological.

**1994 (rupture event):** Acute stressor. Immediate behavioral response is composed — she defends the act publicly and to Hank in coherent ethical terms. There is no acute decompensation visible on-panel. The disorder emerges in the *aftermath*, not in the event.

**1994–1996 (acute adjustment phase):** Symptomatic presentation as described above. Function preserved in vocational domain; contraction in relational/affective domain. Appearances become more transactional.

**Mid-1996 onward (chronic-residual phase):** Stabilization at the contracted baseline. No further deterioration; no remission to premorbid baseline. The picture is best characterized as **a new stable equilibrium below the previous one**, organized around the unresolved moral injury and maintained by occupational hyperengagement.

**Prognosis:** Without intervention — and there is no indication she would seek any, as she does not present to herself as ill — the equilibrium is sustainable indefinitely. With intervention, the moral-injury structure is the appropriate target; standard depression treatments would be poorly matched and likely to produce iatrogenic effects (e.g., a course of cognitive restructuring that attempted to dispute her interpretation of the disclosure's harm would either fail or, if successful, would feel to her like a second moral betrayal). The therapeutically correct approach is acceptance-and-commitment-flavored work on holding the contradiction with less affective cost, plus narrative/meaning-making work on integrating the act into a continuous self-story. She would likely be a good candidate; she is reflective, verbally adept, and not defended against the material — she has simply not been offered a useful structure for it.

---

## 4. DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT SHE IS NOT, AND WHY

The differential is where the file earns its keep. Each category below has been considered and ruled out on specified grounds.

### 4.1 Major Depressive Disorder — RULED OUT

The post-1994 picture superficially resembles depression: social withdrawal, narrowed affect, increased work focus. The differential rests on the absence of *clinical* depressive features: no anhedonia (she takes evident satisfaction in good reporting), no vegetative signs in record, no suicidal ideation, no cognitive triad of worthlessness/hopelessness/helplessness, no diurnal mood variation, no impaired concentration on work tasks. The mood disturbance is **stimulus-tethered** rather than pervasive — it activates on Hank-related material and Legacy-praise stimuli but does not color her engagement with other domains. MDD does not behave this way; it generalizes.

### 4.2 Persistent Depressive Disorder (Dysthymia) — RULED OUT

Requires two-year duration of depressed mood more days than not. The record does not support pervasive dysphoria; it supports a *contracted affective range* with preserved capacity for engagement in non-wounded domains. Dysthymia is a coloring of the whole field; her presentation is a specific lesion.

### 4.3 Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder — RULED OUT

Despite Genosha, Onslaught, Zero Tolerance, and recurrent on-scene mass-casualty exposure, no PTSD signature is present. Required Criterion B (intrusion) symptoms absent: no flashbacks, no nightmares, no intrusive imagery in record. Criterion C (avoidance) absent: she continues to cover mutant affairs, the most reliable source of triggers possible. Criterion D (negative cognitions/mood) — *partially* present but only with respect to the Legacy event, not with respect to the trauma exposures. Criterion E (arousal) absent at clinical threshold; her hyper-alertness is occupational not pathological. The combat-correspondent or war-reporter PTSD pattern is *not* her picture. She is the rarer case of the war reporter who does not develop PTSD because her defense structure (intellectualization, moral framing, sublimation into reporting) is exquisitely well-matched to the role.

### 4.4 Complex PTSD (ICD-11) — RULED OUT

Requires PTSD core plus disturbances in self-organization (affect dysregulation, negative self-concept, interpersonal disturbance). Self-concept stable; affect regulated; interpersonal pattern direct and competent. No basis.

### 4.5 Generalized Anxiety Disorder — RULED OUT

No excessive worry across domains. Operational vigilance is task-specific and resolves with task completion.

### 4.6 Panic Disorder — RULED OUT

No panic episodes in record.

### 4.7 Social Anxiety Disorder — RULED OUT (and quasi-paradoxically)

Her occupation requires daily voluntary entry into high-evaluation contexts (live broadcast, hostile interviews). Performance is composed. No basis.

### 4.8 Obsessive-Compulsive Disorder — RULED OUT

Conscientiousness and thoroughness in reporting are trait-level, not symptom-level. No compulsions, no ego-dystonic obsessions, no ritualized behaviors.

### 4.9 Bipolar Spectrum Disorders — RULED OUT

No depicted manic, hypomanic, or mixed episodes. Energy level high but stable. No depicted impulsive financial, sexual, or grandiose behaviors. The Legacy disclosure was decisive but deliberated within her ethical frame, not impulsive.

### 4.10 Borderline Personality Disorder — RULED OUT, EMPHATICALLY

Despite a high-profile romantic rupture and persistent affective residue, none of the BPD signature features are present. No identity disturbance — her sense of self is stable across the entire record. No splitting — she does not idealize-then-devalue Hank; she sustains a complex view of him as loved and as someone she harmed. No frantic efforts to avoid abandonment — she neither pursued Hank after the rupture nor punished him for leaving. No interpersonal chaos — her professional relationships are durable and her social pattern is consistent. No impulsivity, no self-harm, no chronic emptiness. The differential against BPD is one of the cleanest in the file precisely because the rupture event would, in a BPD presentation, have produced fireworks; in her case it produced a contained, principled, grief-laden withdrawal. That difference *is* the differential.

### 4.11 Narcissistic Personality Disorder — RULED OUT

No grandiosity, no need for admiration (she tolerates being scooped without depicted distress), no lack of empathy (her interview style is empathic), no exploitation pattern. The Legacy disclosure was *not* a narcissistic act — a narcissistic actor would have framed it around her own ethical heroism; she framed it around the public's right to information and accepted the personal cost without compensatory self-aggrandizement.

### 4.12 Histrionic Personality Disorder — RULED OUT

On-camera affect is contained, not theatrical. Off-camera presentation is direct, not seductive or attention-seeking. The vocation involves public visibility but her *use* of that visibility is informational, not exhibitionistic.

### 4.13 Avoidant Personality Disorder — RULED OUT

She pursues hard relationships, hard stories, hostile interviews. The post-rupture relational contraction is **grief-driven foreclosure**, not characterological avoidance. The distinction matters: avoidant patients have *always* been this way; she became this way in response to a specific event and was demonstrably otherwise before it.

### 4.14 Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder — RULED OUT

High conscientiousness and ethical rigidity superficially suggest OCPD. The differential rests on *flexibility*: OCPD patients are rigid across contexts and resistant to alternate frames; she is rigid only on core ethical commitments (do not suppress truth) and is otherwise flexible, humorous, capable of warmth and play (pre-rupture record especially). OCPD is a personality-wide constriction; her constriction is principled and domain-specific.

### 4.15 Dependent Personality Disorder — RULED OUT

The post-rupture failure to recouple could be misread as dependent attachment to the lost object. The reverse is true: a dependent presentation would have rapidly transferred the attachment to a replacement figure. She did not. The non-recoupling indicates *independence from* the need for partnered identity, not pathological dependence on the lost one.

### 4.16 Adjustment Disorder, Acute — SUPERSEDED

The acute adjustment diagnosis applied 1994–1996 and is now in residual phase as documented above.

### 4.17 Substance Use Disorders — RULED OUT

No depicted use beyond social. No escalation under stress.

### 4.18 Somatic Symptom and Related Disorders — RULED OUT

No somatization. Notable given the stress profile.

### 4.19 Dissociative Disorders — RULED OUT

No dissociative episodes in record. Under acute stress (Legacy decision, breakup) she remained verbally present and cognitively integrated.

### 4.20 Adjustment Disorder vs. Normal Grief — THE FINEST CUT

The most important differential in the file is between *psychiatric disorder* and *appropriate response to a hard fact*. The conservative reading is that the Subject's late presentation is not pathology but proportionate adult response to having done something she believed right at irrecoverable cost. The DSM itself increasingly accommodates this distinction (the bereavement exclusion debate, the V-code culture). The most honest formulation in the file is:

> **Subject does not meet criteria for any active DSM-5/ICD-11 disorder. She presents with residual features of a resolved adjustment reaction, subclinical prolonged-grief features, and a structural moral injury organized around a single 1994 event. These features are clinically detectable but functionally compensated. She is not ill. She is wounded, and has elected — competently, with insight, and at preserved cost to her affective range — to live in the wound rather than resolve it on terms she would experience as dishonest.**

That formulation is the diagnosis. The differential is the work that earns the right to it.

---

## 5. RISK ASSESSMENT

- **Suicide risk:** Low. No ideation in record, no prior attempts, protective factors strong (vocation, meaning-structure, ego strength).
- **Self-harm risk:** Negligible.
- **Risk to others:** Negligible in any personal sense. *Professional* risk to others — i.e., the willingness to publish information that produces third-party harm — is real, demonstrated, and would be repeated under analogous circumstances. This is not pathology; it is her ethic. Any operational planning involving Subject must treat this as a fixed parameter, not a behavior to be modified.
- **Decompensation risk:** Moderate under specific conditions — loss of vocational role, forced sustained proximity to Hank without role buffer, public moral attack on the Legacy disclosure (would activate the moral-injury structure under unfavorable conditions). Low under ordinary conditions.
- **Treatment-seeking probability:** Low absent further stressor. She does not present to herself as needing care.

---

## 6. FINAL CLINICAL FORMULATION

A constitutionally high-functioning adult of above-average ego strength, mature defense structure, and unusual moral seriousness, who sustained a single catastrophic moral-relational injury in 1994 and has organized her subsequent life around the unresolved contradiction it produced. No active psychiatric disorder. Residual subclinical features etiologically continuous with that event. Differential clean against the major Axis I and Axis II categories. Prognosis stable at current equilibrium. The case is interesting clinically precisely because it is *not* a case of illness — it is a case of an honest person carrying the actual weight of an honest act, declining the available consolations, and going to work.


## Behavioral Atlas

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: TRISH TILBY
## Section VI — Behavioral Atlas

A surveillance-grade catalog of micro-behavior, decision habits, and somatic tells across the full state-space of her observable life. Each entry derives from canonical depiction (Simonson, David, Lobdell, Nicieza X-Factor and X-Men runs, c. 1988–1999) and from inference disciplined by that record. Where a tell is reconstructed rather than directly shown, it is flagged.

---

### 1. BASELINE — THE WORKING-DAY TRISH

**Posture and carriage.** Upright but not military; weight distributed slightly forward on the balls of the feet — the carriage of someone who anticipates having to move toward something. When standing in conversation she occupies a position roughly fifteen degrees off-square to her interlocutor: not face-on (which reads as confrontation or flirtation, both of which she modulates deliberately), not parallel (which reads as passive). This three-quarter stance is the journalist's interview angle, retained off-duty.

**Hands.** Habitually occupied. Reporter's notebook, pen, microphone, coffee, a phone receiver, a steering wheel, the strap of a shoulder bag — there is almost no panel in the record in which her hands are at rest by her sides. When nothing else is available she will run a fingertip along the edge of a tabletop or hook her thumb into her belt or jacket pocket. **Empty hands are her tell for off-balance**; on the very rare panels where her arms hang straight, something has gone wrong in the scene.

**Gaze.** Long fixations, not many of them. She does not sweep a room; she selects and dwells. Eye contact in conversation runs roughly seventy-thirty in her favor — she gives less than she takes, which is the trained habit of someone whose job is reading faces while keeping her own legible only on her terms. She blinks less than baseline when listening attentively and more than baseline when she has decided the speaker is lying. (The blink-rate uptick is a poker leak; she does not appear aware of it.)

**Voice.** Mid-range, slightly forward in the mask, with the trained breath control of broadcast work. She does not raise her volume to compete; she lowers her register and *slows*, which forces the room to lean in. The voice she uses on-camera is roughly one-third of a step higher and noticeably warmer than her actual conversational voice — the "Trish Tilby" voice and the Trish voice are distinguishable to anyone who has heard both.

**Vocabulary.** Wide, fast, syntactically clean. She avoids journalistic clichés in private speech (she has heard them too often) and reaches by preference for specific nouns over general ones. Profanity is used sparingly and to mark seriousness, not to vent.

**Dress.** Professional, fitted, color-blocked rather than patterned; the working wardrobe optimized for the camera's tolerances — solid jewel tones, no busy weaves, hair pulled back enough to keep out of the shot. Off-camera she relaxes the silhouette but rarely abandons structure entirely. She does not dress to be looked at; she dresses to be *trusted on first glance*, which is a related but distinct optimization.

**Caffeine, food, sleep.** Coffee throughout the day, often not finished — the cup is a prop as much as a stimulant. Eats irregularly and quickly when working, properly and slowly when not. Sleep cadence (inferred) is broadcast-irregular: early-morning calls, late-night edits, recovery in compressed bursts. She is depicted as functional on this regimen, which is itself a tell — she has been doing it long enough that her physiology has adapted.

---

### 2. CALM / LOW-STAKES OBSERVATION

In conditions of genuine ease — Sunday-morning kitchen scenes with Hank, post-deadline drinks with colleagues — the behavioral envelope visibly widens.

- **Sentences grow longer and more digressive.** Working-Trish speaks in headlines; resting-Trish speaks in paragraphs, with embedded clauses and self-interruption. She thinks out loud when safe.
- **Laughter.** Audible and unguarded. She laughs with her whole chest, briefly, then closes it back down — never a sustained giggle, never performed warmth.
- **Cooking behavior.** Depicted competent in the kitchen, prefers to be in motion while talking, will hand off a task to a partner to keep the conversation balanced (she does not like being talked *at* while she works alone).
- **Reading.** A long-form reader; books and newspapers, both. Marginalia behavior implied by her habit of citing specific passages back to interlocutors days after first encounter — she is annotating, mentally if not physically.
- **Touch.** With trusted intimates, freely and absently — a hand on the small of the back passing in a hallway, fingers running along the back of a neck while reading over a shoulder. She does not require touch but offers it constantly when relaxed. Withdrawal of casual touch is her earliest tell that something is wrong between her and a partner.

---

### 3. WORKING STATE — THE FIELD

The reporter on-scene is a distinct operational mode.

- **Approach pattern.** She does not run toward an event; she *walks fast* with the cameraman in tow, scanning for the credentialed authority figure to whom she will direct her first question. The first question is almost always factual and answerable — designed to establish that she is reasonable before she becomes difficult.
- **Microphone discipline.** She holds the mic low when listening and brings it up only when the subject is mid-thought, which yields cleaner audio and signals to the subject that she expects continuation. This is a small craft tell that distinguishes her from less experienced field reporters in the same scenes.
- **Positioning under chaos.** In high-casualty environments (Genosha, Onslaught NYC, Zero Tolerance), she repeatedly chooses cover that preserves a sightline. She is the journalist who survives because she will not stand in the open for a better shot, but she will stand at the edge of cover for as long as the shot lasts. The discipline is **maximal acceptable risk, not maximal risk**.
- **Threat-assessment cadence.** Approximately every fifteen to thirty seconds in an active scene she breaks from her subject to scan — a brief head-turn, a glance at the cameraman, a check of egress. This is internalized and looks like a verbal tic (the pause), but it is spatial.
- **Source handling.** Treats sources with a respect that scales inverse to their power. Junior staffers, secretaries, beat cops, hospital techs — handled with warmth, remembered by name, called back to thank. Senior officials handled cordially but without deference. This is both ethical and tactical: her best information comes from below, and she knows it.
- **Notebook habit.** Takes notes selectively, not continuously. The note she writes is often the one she wants the subject to *see* her writing — a flag that the previous statement has registered. Her actual recall is largely memorial, supplemented by tape.

---

### 4. STRESS — ACUTE

Distinguished here from threat. Stress is deadline, conflict, ethical pressure, time-compressed decision-making.

- **Narrowing.** Pupils, attention, body posture. She loses peripheral sociability — colleagues are addressed by last name, pleasantries vanish, transitional phrases drop out of her speech. Sentences become imperatives.
- **Pace increases, volume does not.** A consistent tell. Where most stressed speakers get louder, she gets *faster and quieter*, which is more difficult to interrupt and harder to read.
- **Decision speed.** Compressed dramatically. The Legacy disclosure decision is the canonical instance: presented with verified information and a window, she resolved within what the record suggests was hours, not days. She does not poll. She does not seek permission. Under acute stress she **stops consulting** — a known failure mode, and the one that broke her relationship.
- **Physical tells.** A characteristic press of the tongue against the inside of the cheek when weighing; a single sharp exhale when decided. The jaw sets; the shoulders drop *down*, not up (trained — broadcast posture under pressure).
- **What she does not do.** Pace. Fidget overtly. Talk to herself. Call for backup. Cry. Eat. Drink (caffeine, alcohol, water — she stops ingesting during acute decision windows, an interesting somatic signature).

---

### 5. STRESS — CHRONIC

The pattern of the post-Legacy years.

- **Field hours expand.** She is on-scene more, in-studio less, in her apartment least. Work as binding agent.
- **Social field contracts.** Fewer named colleagues in later appearances; the dinner-with-friends register disappears almost entirely from the record. She does not announce withdrawal; she simply stops being depicted in those rooms.
- **Affect flattens by a quarter-step.** Not depressed — *muted*. The laugh is shorter. The off-camera voice and the on-camera voice converge: the warmth differential narrows. She is becoming the role more completely because the role is what is left intact.
- **Sleep (inferred) degrades.** Eye area depicted with subtle shadowing in late-canon appearances; this is partly artist drift but consistent enough across hands to read as intentional.
- **Eating habits drift toward the work-desk standard.** Coffee, takeaway, irregular. The Sunday-kitchen Trish does not reappear.
- **No substance escalation.** Notably. She does not drink her way through it. The discipline holds.

---

### 6. THREAT — DIRECT PHYSICAL DANGER

- **First-second response: orientation, not flight.** She turns *toward* the threat to identify it before moving. This is trained behavior — you cannot evade what you have not located — and it distinguishes her from civilian baseline.
- **Second-second response: egress check.** A glance back along her arrival vector.
- **Action.** Move to cover, *retain equipment* (microphone, notebook, recorder — she has been observed clutching her tools through scrambles for cover; they are not optional to her). If the cameraman is with her, she will verbally locate him; she does not abandon crew.
- **Voice under threat.** Drops in pitch, gains in clarity. She gives directions to her cameraman in single words.
- **Post-threat.** No visible shake. A long exhale, a brief closing of the eyes, then she reaches for the notebook. The processing is **immediately reportorial** — she is already writing the lede in her head before her heart rate has come down. This is either healthy occupational integration or a sublimation reflex so well-grooved that grief has no place to land. Probably both.

---

### 7. INTIMACY — ESTABLISHED PARTNERSHIP (THE HANK YEARS)

- **Greeting ritual.** When entering a shared space where the partner is present, she announces verbally rather than physically — voice from the hallway before her body in the room. This is consideration (he startles less) and also a small power move (she controls the moment of mutual orientation).
- **Bedroom-to-kitchen patterns.** Domestic scenes show her comfortable in others' bathrobes, drinking from his mug, reading his correspondence at the breakfast table without asking. The boundary porosity is intentional — she is signaling that the relationship has no edges she respects, which is intimacy as policy.
- **Argument style.** Direct, fast, lexically precise. She names the thing rather than circling it. She will interrupt but stops when called on it. She does not stonewall; the silence treatment is not in her repertoire. She does, however, *reframe* mid-argument — moving the dispute up an abstraction level, which can feel to a partner like a goalpost shift but is actually her cognitive style asserting itself under pressure.
- **Repair behavior.** Quick to initiate, slow to fully concede. She will return to the room within the hour, offer the gesture of contact (a hand on the arm, a coffee placed in front of him), and resume function — but the substantive position is rarely surrendered. She repairs the *bond* without revising the *argument*. This works as long as the argument was about something both parties can live with.
- **Sexual register (inferred from depicted comfort and the absence of somatic-disgust signaling around Hank's nonhuman body).** Unselfconscious, integrated with the relationship's verbal play, untroubled by the partner's morphology. She is not exoticizing and she is not pretending; she is simply *with him*. The capacity to be physically present to a body most of the world would flinch from is one of the deepest character facts in her record.
- **Tells of declining intimacy (late in the relationship, pre-rupture).** Reduced casual touch in transit through shared spaces. Phone calls returned, not initiated. Eating separately when both are home. Conversation pivoting to work topics by default. These are the standard markers; she shows them in the weeks-equivalent before the Legacy decision but does not name them.

---

### 8. INTIMACY — POST-RUPTURE

- **In Hank's presence (professional contexts).** Stance squares up an additional five degrees toward face-on — she does not allow herself the three-quarter angle with him, because the three-quarter angle is for interviewing strangers and he is not a stranger. Voice flattens to her professional register, then breaks into something briefly warmer on the third or fourth exchange, then recovers. She does not initiate touch. She does not avoid his eye but she also does not hold it.
- **Post-encounter.** Goes back to work faster than the situation warrants. No depicted catharsis. The processing is private and never shown on-panel, which is itself the point — she has elected to keep it interior.
- **New partners (Trevor Chase and the managerial-orbit figures).** Engaged but not invested. The depicted register is *companionable*, not committed. She is functional with these partners and not transformed by them. The relationship-shaped space in her life is occupied without being filled.

---

### 9. GRIEF

She does not perform grief. The grief signatures are *negative space* — what stops happening rather than what starts.

- **Crying.** Rare, brief, contained. The post-disclosure breakup scene contains the most affective depiction in her record and even there she does not collapse — she weeps while still upright, still speaking, still defending her position.
- **The Sunday morning.** What disappears from her life after Hank is the long unstructured private hour. Late-canon Trish is never depicted in the quiet domestic register. The absence is the grief.
- **Anniversaries (inferred).** No on-panel depiction, but the pattern of her late-canon appearances suggests a working journalist who has tuned her calendar to avoid the dates that would require sitting still with the loss. She schedules into them.
- **Reminders.** She manages them. A Beast headline, a McCoy quote in a press release, a glimpse on the wire — she processes the spike privately and moves on within seconds. The face holds. The blink rate goes up briefly.
- **Conversations about Hank.** She permits them and does not redirect. She speaks of him accurately and without bitterness. The lack of bitterness is the most psychiatrically significant tell in her late record — she has not split him into a villain to ease her grief, which means she is metabolizing the contradiction *in real time, indefinitely*. This is exhausting; it is also the thing that keeps her recognizably herself.

---

### 10. VICTORY

Professional wins (scoops, broken stories, exclusive interviews) are handled with a notable understatement.

- **No celebration.** A nod to the producer, a brief sit-down with the cameraman, a single drink. She does not crow.
- **Immediate next-question behavior.** Within minutes of landing a story she is asking what the follow-up is. The win is a platform, not a destination.
- **The Legacy story is the exception that proves the rule.** She did not celebrate it. She defended it. The structural ambiguity of the win — public service, private catastrophe — short-circuited her usual response, and she has not had an unambiguous large-scale victory in the record since against which to recalibrate.
- **Praise tolerance.** Low. She redirects compliments to the team, to the source, to the timing. This is not false modesty; it is **discomfort with being the subject** — a trained inversion of her instrument. She is in the business of pointing the camera at other people and the camera turned around is the camera misused.

---

### 11. DEFEAT

Distinguished from grief: defeat is the lost story, the killed segment, the source who burned her, the rival who scooped her.

- **First response: forensic.** *What did I miss.* She walks back her own work, names the error, files it. No blame externalized that is not earned.
- **Second response: targeted.** She does not generalize "I am bad at this." She isolates the failure and adjusts the specific habit that produced it.
- **Visible affect.** A brief tightening around the eyes; a longer-than-usual exhale; a quiet hour. Then back to work.
- **Grudges.** She holds them quietly and proportionately. She does not retaliate; she also does not forget. A burned source does not get called again. A rival who played dirty gets denied courtesy without being denied professionalism.
- **Failure she cannot fix.** This is where her defense structure thins. The defeats that cannot be metabolized into improvement — the Legacy fallout being the prototype — become the moral-injury residue. She handles fixable defeat exceptionally well; she handles unfixable defeat by working *around* it indefinitely.

---

### 12. DECEPTION — DETECTING AND PRODUCING

- **Detecting.** Her interview style is built on the slow pressure of patient repetition. She will return to a question three or four times across an interview in slightly different framings, comparing the answers. The blink-rate uptick she shows when she has decided a subject is lying is followed, often within the same beat, by a slight forward lean and a softening of voice — *she gets warmer when she catches you*, because she wants you to keep talking. This is one of her most effective working behaviors.
- **Producing.** She does not lie. She withholds, frames, and selects. She will decline to answer a question rather than answer it falsely, even in private. The deontological floor extends to her own utterances, not just to her broadcasts. This is, again, expensive — it costs her social ease — and it is structural to her identity.

---

### 13. ROUTES, RITUALS, MICRO-HABITS

- **Commute.** Implied urban — she lives within the broadcast footprint and moves on foot, by cab, by car-service. She is not depicted driving long distances; her geography is dense and walkable.
- **Coffee.** Two minimum before going on air. The first is functional; the second is ritual. She holds the second cup longer than she drinks from it.
- **Phone behavior.** Returns calls in batches, not as they come. Prefers in-person over phone over voicemail. Will let a phone ring if mid-thought; does not treat the device as authoritative.
- **Email/digital (modernized read).** Inbox-zero by discipline; uses the inbox as a queue, not an archive. Filed correspondence by source and by story, cross-referenced. The professional organizational habit is high.
- **The notebook.** A specific kind, replaced when filled, dated on the cover, archived. She can almost certainly produce any working note from the last decade within minutes. The notebooks are her external memory and she treats them as such.
- **Dress ritual before going on air.** A check in mirror — earrings, collar, hair, *eyes* (she checks her own eyes, not for makeup but for alertness; if she doesn't like what she sees she does breathwork before going live).
- **End-of-day.** Removes shoes within seconds of entering her apartment. Sits *down* before doing anything else for approximately ninety seconds — a deliberate decompression beat. Then up, and into the evening. The ninety-second sit is one of the few self-care rituals she preserves across all eras of the record.

---

### 14. TELLS BY CATEGORY — QUICK REFERENCE

- **She is uncertain when:** her hands are empty and her sentences shorten.
- **She is angry when:** her voice drops and her pace increases.
- **She has decided when:** she exhales sharply once, jaw sets, shoulders drop.
- **She is lying to herself when:** she reframes upward — moves a concrete question to abstract ethical ground without being asked.
- **She has caught you lying when:** blink rate spikes, then she gets warmer.
- **She is grieving when:** the long private hours disappear from her schedule.
- **She is in love when:** she leaves her things in your space without asking.
- **She is done with you when:** she returns calls but does not initiate them.
- **She is at her best when:** the ethical structure of a situation is clear and the tactical structure is hard. She lives for that combination.
- **She is at her worst when:** the ethical structure of a situation is clear and the *cost* is private. That is where she breaks her own heart and keeps going.

---

### 15. SUMMARY OBSERVATION

The behavioral signature is unified by a single principle: **she is always working, in the sense that she is always reading the room for what is true and what is being concealed, and she is always governed by a deontological commitment that subordinates her own comfort to that reading**. The micro-tells, the routes, the rituals, the intimacies all rhyme with this. She is not opaque — she is, in fact, unusually legible to anyone willing to watch — but she is *consistent*, and that consistency is what makes her dangerous to lie to, durable under fire, and unable to forgive herself for the one act of which she remains most professionally proud.

The Atlas closes where the file does: on a woman who has not changed her habits since the rupture because the habits are what she has instead of resolution.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: TRISH TILBY
## Section 6 — Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

*What a week of surveillance would record. Granular, longitudinal, with era-flags where the pattern shifts.*

---

## 6.1 The Architecture of a Day (Baseline, c. 1991–1993, "Hank Era")

The defining structural fact of Subject's daily life is that she runs on a **broadcast clock, not a solar clock**. Her hours are organized around two anchor points: the morning editorial meeting (roughly 0930 in her newsroom's known cadence) and the evening broadcast (variously 1800 or 2200 depending on assignment cycle). Everything between and around these is plastic, but the anchors are inviolable; she is on time to both, every observed instance, including those documented during active mutant crises in which the city around her was, in narrative terms, on fire.

**Wake.** Estimated 0615–0645, no alarm visible in residential beats but the consistency suggests one set and obeyed. Subject is not a snoozer; the depicted morning shots show her already vertical, already moving. There is no on-panel evidence of a meditation, journaling, or stretching practice. The morning ritual is **information-first**: she is at the radio/television before she is at the coffee. The pattern is consistent with reporters who have trained themselves to absorb the overnight news cycle before forming any independent thought about the day, on the theory that one cannot be scooped on a story one already knows broke.

**Coffee.** Coffee is taken black, in volume, and continuously. It is not a ritual object for her — there is no fetishization of the cup, the bean, the method — it is fuel and metronome. The mug is whatever mug is closest. During the cohabitation period with McCoy, the refill cadence is observably elevated because McCoy makes a fresh pot whenever he sees hers cooling; she does not refuse and does not thank him for it after the first month, which is the small marker of domesticity having taken root.

**Dress.** Working wardrobe is a small, deliberate rotation: blazers in three or four neutral tones, blouses, trousers more often than skirts, low heels she can actually run in. The signature is **functional unfussiness**: she dresses to be taken seriously on camera and to chase a source down a corridor in the same outfit. Jewelry is minimal — small earrings, a watch (analog, kept to the second; she sets it against the network time signal). Makeup is applied for camera and refreshed in cabs; off-camera weekends she wears markedly less. Hair maintenance is a known cost center — observed appointments at regular intervals, because the on-air look has tolerances.

**Commute.** Cab, subway, or a station car depending on assignment; not depicted to drive recreationally. Reads two papers in transit, physical newsprint, folding them in the precise quarter-fold of the practiced subway reader. Does not wear headphones — the deliberate maintenance of ambient hearing in public space is consistent with her **threat-awareness profile** (see §2: the woman who survives Onslaught NYC without injury is the woman who hears what's behind her).

---

## 6.2 The Workday in Granular Detail

**Newsroom arrival, ~0900.** First stop is not her desk; it is the assignment editor's desk, then the wire terminals. She inspects the overnight queue herself rather than relying on the producer's summary — a small but telling distrust of mediated information that runs through her entire professional carriage.

**Morning meeting, ~0930.** Subject is a known speaker in meetings — not a dominator but a definer. The behavioral pattern is to listen to two or three rounds of editorial pitching, then offer a reframe: not "I have a story," but "the story here is X." Colleagues over the years would describe her, if pressed, as the person who names what the room is actually talking about. This is the same cognitive habit (moral-frame-first, see §3) operating in low-stakes meeting register.

**Desk hours, late morning to early afternoon.** Phone work. Subject is a **telephone reporter** in the classical sense — long calls, source maintenance, the slow daily upkeep of a network that took years to build. She keeps a Rolodex (era-appropriate; transitions to a desk organizer and later a digital contacts file by the late nineties) that is observed to be physically thick and color-tabbed. The system is hers; nobody else can use it. She does not let assistants make her calls. Source-handling style is **patient, conversational, non-transactional in tone but transactional in fact** — she will spend twenty minutes on a source's divorce before she gets to the question, and the question, when it comes, is framed as if she already knows the answer and only wants confirmation. Sources rarely realize how much they have told her until they see it on air.

**Lunch.** Working lunch by default — sandwich at the desk, or a brief sit-down with a source at a midprice restaurant within four blocks of the building. Subject has two or three habitual lunch venues she uses for source meetings, chosen for **acoustic privacy** (booths, ambient noise high enough to defeat eavesdropping, staff who do not hover). She tips generously and consistently at these places, which is operational hygiene as much as character — she needs to remain welcome and remain forgotten.

**Field work, afternoon.** When on a story she is out, fast. Field carriage is distinctive: she walks at a brisk professional clip but does not run unless something is on fire; she carries a small bag (notebook, recorder, pens, extra batteries, a folded copy of the day's wire summary, sometimes a paperback for waits); she stations herself at the **margin** of a scene rather than the center, because the margin is where civilians and lower-rank officials drift to and become talkative. She does not jostle the front line of the press scrum. This is partly temperament and partly tactic — she has learned that the third question in a press conference is more answerable than the first.

**Filing and edit, late afternoon.** Subject writes her own copy and resists rewrites. Observed behavior in edit bays shows her standing behind the editor, not sitting beside — a small dominance cue that producers learn to either accommodate or contest. She is exacting about word choice on mutant-affairs stories specifically: she will not use the word "menace," she will not use "creature," she pushes back on chyrons that pre-judge. This is the **deontological-journalist ethic** (§5) operating at the level of the syllable.

**Broadcast.** On-air she is contained, articulate, slightly faster-tempo than network average. She holds eye contact with the camera as if with a single specific person. Off-camera between live hits she is observed to drop the on-air register entirely — quieter voice, looser posture, dry humor with the crew. The professional mask is real and is taken off and put on as needed; it is not load-bearing for her identity (see §3 on performative-cognitive self-concept: the mask is the *instrument*, not the *self*).

**Post-broadcast wind-down.** Brief debrief with the producer, brief drink with one or two colleagues at a known bar near the building (a glass and a half of white wine, not more, on a weeknight; she has observably learned where her limit is and stays a notch below it), then home or to McCoy's during the cohabitation period.

---

## 6.3 Evenings — The "Hank Era" Texture (c. 1990–1994)

This is the warmest and most documented section of the record. A week of surveillance during this period would log a domestic life of unusual mundanity for the X-corpus:

- **Cooking together** is a recurring depicted activity. Neither is a serious cook; the texture is more "two professionals making pasta and arguing about an article" than gastronomy. Subject is comfortable in a kitchen but does not appear to find it restorative; the cooking is a vehicle for the conversation.
- **Reading in the same room** is the modal evening activity. She reads work (transcripts, background files, fiction in narrow windows); McCoy reads science. They do not require continuous interaction; the capacity to be quiet together is a marker of the relationship's actual depth.
- **Music** is a low-grade constant. Subject's taste runs to jazz and singer-songwriter material, often on in the background; she does not appear to attend live music regularly.
- **Television** is on for news and not much else. She does not appear to watch entertainment programming with any regularity, which is partly professional contempt (she knows how the sausage is made) and partly the workaholic's foreshortened leisure horizon.
- **Sex life** is depicted as healthy and integrated; see §2. The relevant behavioral note is that intimacy was not bracketed off from the workday — affection and argument and editorial debate occurred in the same evening, in the same room, without compartmentalization. This is consistent with secure attachment functioning.
- **Sleep.** Estimated 2330–0030 lights-out on weeknights, with the late-broadcast nights pushing past 0100. Wakes early regardless. She is running a sleep debt for which she compensates on weekends with one long morning.

**Argument pattern, observed:** Subject argues face-on, in the same room, until resolved or exhausted; she does not withdraw or stonewall. The argument style is **verbal, pointed, occasionally cutting in word choice but never escalatory in volume**. Recovery is fast — she will be civil within the hour and warm within the evening. This pattern is what allows the relationship to absorb the high friction of two demanding careers. It is also what makes the Legacy rupture so total: she had no script for a fight that did not resolve.

---

## 6.4 Rituals (Standing Weekly and Annual)

**Standing weekly:**

- **Sunday morning long-read.** The one observed reliably leisured window — late wake, full breakfast, the Sunday papers consumed cover-to-cover over two or three hours, often in a robe at a kitchen table. This is the closest thing she has to a sabbath. The ritual survives the breakup; in the post-Hank record she still has Sundays, just alone.
- **Friday post-broadcast drink** with one or two newsroom colleagues, as above. Not negotiable; canceled only for breaking news.
- **Source maintenance calls** on a rough rotation — observed pattern is that she touches base with key sources at intervals calibrated to each (weekly for hot, monthly for warm, quarterly for cold), and she remembers their children's names, their surgeries, their team allegiances. This is a discipline, not a gift; she keeps notes.

**Standing annual:**

- Subject is not depicted observing major holidays with religious content. Thanksgiving and Christmas appear in the record as relationship beats, not theological ones — meals with McCoy and, at least once, with elements of the X-Factor circle, navigated with reportorial poise (she is the only non-mutant at the table and behaves as if this is unremarkable).
- Birthdays are observed but not made central. She gives gifts that are specific and considered (a book the recipient has mentioned wanting, a small object tied to an in-joke); she receives them with grace and without performance.

**Idiosyncratic micro-rituals:**

- **The notebook.** A reporter's narrow notebook is in her hand or her bag at all times. Observed to flip it open during conversations of any consequence; she does not ask permission, and the gesture is so habitual that interlocutors stop noticing. Notebooks are dated on the cover and archived; the archive is hers, physically maintained.
- **The pen check.** Before any interview, an observable patdown for pen and recorder. The recorder is checked twice — power, tape/memory — a small compulsive ritual of the burned-once professional.
- **The post-interview walk.** Subject is observed to walk for several blocks after a significant interview before returning to the office, reviewing in her head before committing to paper. This is her **integration interval**; she does not skip it.
- **End-of-day mug rinse.** The last action at her desk is to rinse her coffee mug in the office kitchen and return it upside down on the rack. Small, observed across years. The kind of habit a surveillance file would log without knowing why it logged it.

---

## 6.5 Place Habits — Where She Is, Reliably

A surveillance map of Subject would have a small number of high-confidence pins:

1. **The network building.** Observed five to six days per week, anchor location.
2. **Her residence.** A Manhattan apartment, sized for a single professional, upgraded marginally over the years. During cohabitation, McCoy's residence (variously Ship, the X-Factor complex, later Xavier's grounds — she visits the latter but is not observed to live there) becomes a secondary node.
3. **Two or three habitual restaurants** within four blocks of the network building (source lunches).
4. **One bar** (Friday wind-down, occasional weeknights).
5. **The dry cleaner, the hair salon, the deli** — the unromantic infrastructure of a working woman's week, each on a regular cadence, each within a tight residential perimeter.
6. **A gym or running route** — implied by physical conditioning sustained across years; not heavily depicted but the body that runs from Sentinels does not arrive at the run untrained.
