Drinking increases modestly within the social envelope — wine with dinner becomes wine with dinner plus a second glass after — but does not approach pathological use. Recoil typically resolves over two to six weeks into a new, slightly diminished baseline. The diminishment is permanent but small. Across her published life she has absorbed perhaps a dozen such diminishments; the Legacy disclosure was the only one that triggered Rung 5.

**Rung 5 — Settlement (the contradiction goes structural).** This is what decompensation looks like in her case: not collapse but *settlement*, the conversion of an acute moral injury into a permanent feature of her interior architecture. The acute affect goes underground; the cognitive frame that produced the act remains intact; the relational casualty is mourned but not metabolized. She does not heal because healing would require either recanting the frame (which she cannot do without losing her core identity) or forgiving herself for the harm (which she cannot do without disrespecting the relational stake she lost). She elects the contradiction and lives in it. **The settlement is the decompensation.** It is also the reason she remains functional — the unresolved structure is load-bearing in a perverse way, because it provides a stable container for what would otherwise be free-floating grief.

---

### 2. Decompensation pattern: the contraction signature

If Rung 5 has been triggered, the steady-state pattern that follows is observable and consistent. It is the pattern she enters after the Legacy break and never fully exits.

- **Social field contraction.** Intimate relationships do not reform at the same depth. Acquaintance relationships persist and are maintained with apparent warmth; new intimates are not added. The "girlfriend in the kitchen with Hank" texture of the early record disappears and is not replaced. Brief involvements occur (the Trevor Chase–register figures) but are characterized by low investment on her side and are allowed to die when they die.
- **Domestic deactivation.** The cooking, the cohabiting rhythms, the apartment-as-shared-space texture goes dormant. The space becomes more clearly *operational* — a place to sleep and stage from. She does not become a slob; she becomes a person whose home does not signal hospitality because hospitality is no longer being offered.
- **Vocational hypertrophy.** Work expands to fill the space the relational world vacated. She takes harder beats, longer hours, more travel. The work is genuinely good — she is not phoning it in — but the quantity is medicating something. This is **occupation-as-binding-agent**, the textbook adult-functional response to ungrieved loss.
- **Affective flattening within range.** She remains capable of the full affective spectrum but operates in a narrower band of it. The big laughs are rarer; the cutting humor sharpens. The on-camera affect, always contained, becomes slightly more so — a few degrees cooler. Colleagues who knew her before would note it; colleagues who met her after would not, because the new baseline is internally consistent.
- **Tenderness in the wound's vicinity.** Anything that lands in the cognitive neighborhood of the Hank rupture — the disease/disclosure structure, the love/duty conflict, the journalist-and-subject romance — produces a small pause, a slight withdrawal, a brief lapse in her usual quick conversational return. She does not avoid these topics; she registers them and continues. But the register is observable.
- **Refusal of the easy resolution.** Offered the chance to recant — by sympathetic interlocutors, by professional setbacks, by Hank himself in any reconciliation scene the corpus offers — she does not take it. The refusal is not pride; it is structural. The frame that produced the act is the frame that organizes her selfhood. Recanting would not relieve the grief, it would add to it.

---

### 3. What true collapse would look like

Tilby has not been depicted in true collapse, but the architecture above predicts what it would look like. A total-intelligence file requires the prediction.

**Collapse precondition.** A second Legacy-class event — meaning a situation in which the deontological-journalist frame requires an act whose human cost she can foresee, and the cost lands on someone she loves *and* the act itself turns out to have been built on a factual error. The Legacy disclosure was true; that is what makes it survivable. A *second* such disclosure that turned out to be factually wrong — a story she broke at relational cost that subsequently collapsed under verification — would destroy the load-bearing structure of the Rung 5 settlement. The contradiction she has elected to live in is tolerable because both halves are real. Remove the reality of one half and the architecture has no support.

**Collapse signature.** The first observable would be a **cessation of work**, not an increase. The vocational hypertrophy that has medicated the original wound would no longer function, because the wound's organizing frame would itself be in question. She would not take new assignments, would not return calls, would file no copy. This would persist for days before anyone in her professional orbit registered it as anomalous, because she has no history of erratic behavior to which it could be compared.

**Second observable: domestic dereliction.** The apartment, already operational rather than hospitable, would become unkempt — not squalid, but visibly unattended. Mail would accumulate. Food would not be replaced. She would not stop eating, but the eating would become haphazard and external — takeaway, restaurant, things requiring no decision.

**Third observable: cognitive de-structuring.** This is the most clinically significant. Her cognitive style is integrative and moral-frame-first; in true collapse she would lose the capacity to settle a frame. She would oscillate. She would speak in incomplete sentences not from stress but from genuine inability to land an interpretation. This would be misread by observers as depression, and antidepressants would not touch it because the substrate is not affective but **architectural** — the meaning-making apparatus itself has failed, not the mood regulator.

**Fourth observable: drinking past the envelope.** Not addiction in the formal sense, but the social-drinking baseline would lose its containment. The second glass after dinner that appeared in the Legacy recoil would become a third, a fourth, eventually a bottle. The function would be sedative rather than recreational, and she would know this and continue.

**Fifth observable: relational re-approach, badly aimed.** She would attempt to reconstruct the Hank-equivalent bond, but lacking the original substrate she would choose poorly — a colleague, a source, a stranger — and the attempts would fail in ways that compounded the de-structuring. This is the only register in which she would behave in ways resembling the dramatic decompensations of more affectively volatile personalities, and it would be brief, embarrassing, and uncharacteristic.

**Sixth observable: ideation, not action.** Suicide is unlikely in the active sense; her ego strength and her sense of public role both contraindicate it. But **passive ideation** — wishing for non-being, a diminished investment in self-preservation, lapsed seatbelts and crossings against the light — would appear. She would not name it. It would be detectable only through pattern surveillance over weeks.

**Recovery from true collapse, if it occurred, would require the reconstruction of the moral-cognitive frame itself**, not the soothing of affect. The work would be slow, would not respond to standard pharmacological intervention, and would most likely be accomplished — if at all — through a long return to fieldwork at lowered stakes, in which the integrity of the frame could be tested in small instances until it held weight again. This is months-to-years work. It has not been depicted in the canon because the canon has not put her there.

---

### 4. Conditions that produce the failure

The decompensation pathway above is not reached by ordinary stress, even severe ordinary stress. The conditions are specific and stackable; the more that are present, the higher the rung reached.

1. **A binary moral frame with high stakes on both arms.** She does not break under situations she can metabolize as ethically unilateral. She breaks where duty and love are genuinely opposed, both legibly so, both with real weight.
2. **Time pressure that forecloses deliberation.** Her cognitive style under stress is decisive, not deliberative. Given a week to decide the Legacy question, she might have negotiated a different path. Given hours, she resolved. Compression of the decision window is a multiplier on the failure pathway.
3. **Solitude in the decision moment.** She does not consult under Rung 2 compression. Removing trusted interlocutors from her immediate orbit at the compression moment makes the binary frame harder to soften.
4. **A relational stake she has under-named to herself.** Tilby is verbally fluent but does not narrate her own attachments fully — she enacts them, she does not declaim them. Stakes she has not explicitly articulated are stakes she will under-weight in a frame-compression event, because the compression operates on declared variables. The Hank loss was greater than the version of it she had named to herself before she acted. This is recurring vulnerability.
5. **Subsequent praise for the costly act.** The post-act environment matters. Praise destabilizes worse than censure. Censure she can metabolize against the frame (the frame produced the act and the frame remains); praise re-opens the question of whether the act was *worth* its private cost, and she has no defense against the re-opening because she has not closed it internally. Operational note: anyone wishing to destabilize her does so not by attacking the Legacy decision but by celebrating it warmly and at length.
6. **Reminders of the original wound in unexpected registers.** Direct reminders (a Hank sighting, a Legacy retrospective) she has hardened against. Indirect ones — a colleague's analogous dilemma, a disease-and-disclosure ethics panel, a young reporter asking her about the call — slip past the hardening and produce small recoils. Stacked over a short period, these can move her from Rung 0 baseline to Rung 1 activation without an external story driving the activation, which she will misread as occupational restlessness and respond to with more work, compounding the underlying contraction.
7. **Loss of the press credential.** Hypothetical but structurally important. Her self-concept is portable because the credential is portable. Strip the institutional affiliation — blacklisting, industry collapse, a libel judgment, a regulatory bar — and the **portable self** loses its passport. She would not collapse immediately; she would attempt to freelance, to write long-form, to teach. But the slow erosion of the credentialed role over a sustained period is the single environmental condition most likely to drive her toward the true-collapse signature described above, because it would remove the vocational hypertrophy that medicates the original wound *while leaving the wound intact*.
8. **A factual collapse of a past story.** Discussed above as the collapse precondition. Even a minor instance — a corrected story, a retracted detail — produces disproportionate distress because it threatens the frame on which the larger settlement rests.

---

### 5. Failure modes she does *not* exhibit

The total-intelligence file requires negative space as well as positive. The following decompensation patterns are inconsistent with her architecture and should not be predicted from her file even under severe stress:

- **Acting-out / externalization.** She does not blame, does not scapegoat, does not retaliate. Even post-Legacy, with ample provocation, she did not attack Hank in print or in conversation. This is robust across the record.
- **Somatization.** No conversion symptoms, no stress-driven illness pattern, no hypochondriacal register. The body is not her stress organ.
- **Substance dependence.** Even in the worst projected collapse, the drinking is sedative-instrumental, not addictive in structure. Her relationship to substances is utilitarian.
- **Suicide attempt.** Active self-destruction is contraindicated by her sense of public role and her ego strength. Passive ideation is plausible at full collapse; attempt is not.
- **Florid affective episodes.** No mania, no psychotic break, no panic-disorder presentation. The architecture is too stable for affective storms; what breaks is the cognitive frame, not the mood regulator.
- **Identity diffusion / dependent collapse onto a stronger figure.** She will not become an appendage. Even in the worst case, the bad re-approach attempts described above would be brief and would not produce a sustained merger with another personality.
- **Conversion / radicalization.** She will not abandon the deontological-journalist frame for a consequentialist or partisan one under stress. The frame is too deeply identity-constitutive; abandoning it is not a register her architecture supports. She would sooner stop working than work from a different frame.

---

### 6. Summary

Tilby's failure mode is the failure mode of the **structurally honest**: she breaks where her commitments require her to break, she does not heal where healing would require dishonesty, and she carries the cost as a permanent feature of her interior rather than as an episodic crisis. The five-rung escalation runs from baseline arousal through frame-compression to a costly act and a permanent settlement; true collapse is reachable only by attacking the factual or institutional substrate of the frame itself, and would manifest as cognitive de-structuring rather than affective storm. Standard psychiatric intervention would miss her because she would not present in standard psychiatric registers. What would help her, if anything, is the slow rebuilding of small confirmations that the frame holds — which is to say, the only thing that can repair her is more of the work that wounded her, performed at lower stakes until the architecture re-stabilizes. She knows this. It is why she keeps working.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: TRISH TILBY
## Section 9 — Trajectory & Forward Assessment

---

### Preliminary Frame

Forward assessment of Subject is unusually tractable for an X-corpus civilian, for three reasons. First, her behavioral repertoire is narrow and stable: she does what she does, and she does it the same way across a decade of record. Second, the central wound is identified, named, and *unresolved by choice* — which means the fork points are knowable, because they are the conditions under which the choice would be revisited. Third, she is aging in something close to real time across her published life (estimated mid-thirties at first appearance, estimated late forties to early fifties at the time of this assessment if extrapolated linearly), and the developmental tasks of the next two decades are predictable in the actuarial sense even where the dramatic ones are not.

What follows is structured as: (1) baseline projection assuming no major disruption, (2) the principal fork points where trajectory bifurcates, (3) the growth vector and what it requires, (4) the catastrophe vector and what it looks like, (5) the open questions an intelligence file would actively monitor, and (6) the single-likeliest path on current evidence.

---

### 1. Baseline Projection (No Disruption)

Absent a precipitating event, Subject will continue the trajectory of the late record: deepening expertise on the mutant-affairs beat, increasing institutional weight within whichever outlet retains her (or independent platform if the broadcast model around her continues to erode), narrowing social field, and continuing the low-grade chronic adjustment reaction without it crystallizing into clinical depression.

The professional curve in this scenario is **upward but specialized**. She is by now the dean of her beat — the reporter other reporters call when something breaks they don't understand. This produces a predictable migration: from field correspondent (high-exposure, high-physical-risk) toward analyst/anchor/long-form role (lower exposure, higher cumulative authority). The transition is being forced on her by age and the industry simultaneously; she will resist it cosmetically (she will still go to the scene when she can justify it) but will functionally accept it because the analytic role pays the part of her that has always been moral-frame-first.

The personal curve in this scenario is **flat-to-slow-decline**. She will continue not to remarry, not to partner seriously, not to have children. The window on the last has closed or is closing in the baseline. Friendships will persist — she is not isolated, she is *contracted* — but the inner ring will be small: two or three people, mostly professional contemporaries, none of whom carry the weight Hank carried. She will become the kind of woman whose colleagues describe her as "private" and whose few close friends describe her as "the loyalest person I know." Both are accurate.

The internal curve in this scenario is the one to watch. The unresolved moral injury does not, in baseline, get worse — moral injury is not a progressive condition in the neurodegenerative sense — but it does *calcify*. The longer she lives inside the contradiction without revisiting it, the more the contradiction becomes load-bearing for her identity, and the harder any later attempt at resolution becomes. By her sixties in the baseline, the wound is no longer a wound; it is the shape of the building. This is survivable. It is not flourishing.

**Baseline endpoint, age ~65:** respected, somewhat solitary senior journalist; the dean of her field; the author, eventually, of a long-form book on mutant-affairs reporting that is honest about the Legacy disclosure in the way her on-air work has never been; physically intact, cognitively sharp, emotionally banked. Dies of something ordinary in her late seventies. The obituary leads with the Legacy story. She would have wanted it to lead with something else and would not have been able to say what.

---

### 2. Fork Points

The baseline holds unless one of the following occurs. Each is a discrete event-type with a known psychological signature in Subject's case, and each rotates the trajectory measurably.

**Fork A — Re-encounter with Hank under conditions permitting actual conversation.** The most consequential single variable. Across the late record, their professional crossings have been brief, witnessed, and structurally constrained. A condition that produces sustained private contact — a crisis that throws them together, a deliberate outreach by either party, a mediated reckoning — opens the possibility of the only conversation that could move the wound. The fork is sharp: handled well, it begins the only viable healing arc; handled badly (or refused), it re-traumatizes and accelerates the calcification.

**Fork B — A second event of the Legacy structural type.** A scenario in which she again holds a piece of information whose publication would harm someone she loves but whose suppression would harm a public she serves. The probability of this recurring on her beat is non-trivial; the mutant-affairs landscape generates such dilemmas structurally. How she resolves the *second* instance is the diagnostic test of whether the first was a value she holds or a value she imposed on herself and has been paying for ever since. Either outcome is informative; one is growth, the other is repetition-compulsion in mature-defense clothing.

**Fork C — Public vindication or public repudiation of the Legacy disclosure.** Should the historical record on Legacy shift — should it emerge, for instance, that the disclosure measurably saved lives in human populations through earlier containment, *or* that the disclosure's harms were greater than initially estimated — Subject's moral-injury structure is forced open. Vindication is the more dangerous of the two for her, paradoxically: praise for the act collapses her carefully-maintained equilibrium of "right act, terrible cost" into a register her psyche has no protocol for. Repudiation she could metabolize (it would confirm her grief); vindication would require her to *enjoy* having been right, which is the thing she has been refusing to do for fifteen years.

**Fork D — A serious illness or mortality event in her own body.** Subject's medical sparseness will not last forever; she is in the age band where the actuarial tables begin to assert themselves. A diagnosis of consequence — particularly anything with a treatment arc rather than an acute crisis — forces the inventory questions she has been deferring. Who is the emergency contact. Whose voice does she want. The answer she discovers she wants and the answer she has arranged for are not the same answer, and the gap is data.

**Fork E — A successor / mentee relationship of unusual intensity.** Subject has no children and, in the baseline, will have none. The displacement of generative drive into mentorship is the predictable substitute, and a particular junior reporter — almost certainly a young woman, almost certainly one who reminds her of herself at thirty — could become the relational center of her late career. This is benign and stabilizing if it stays in the mentorship register. It becomes a fork if the mentee faces her own Legacy-structure dilemma and seeks Subject's counsel: Subject's answer to that question is the answer she has been unable to give herself, and giving it aloud is the beginning of resolution.

**Fork F — Industry collapse / platform loss.** The portable self that her press credential provides is contingent on the institution backing the credential. A scenario in which she loses platform — outlet folds, beat is eliminated, she is pushed out for being expensive and aging — removes the identity-stabilizer she has leaned on for thirty years. This is a high-danger fork. The catastrophe vector below runs through it.

**Fork G — Death of Hank.** The terminal version of Fork A. If he predeceases her without the conversation having occurred, the wound becomes uncloseable. This is the single worst input to her future and the one she has the least control over.

---

### 3. The Growth Vector

Growth, for Subject, does not look like becoming a different person. She is, by the assessment of every preceding section, a person of high baseline function whose principal pathology is a chosen unresolution. Growth looks like *electing differently on the unresolution*.

The mechanism would require, in sequence:

1. **A safe-enough conversation with Hank** in which both parties have aged sufficiently past the acute injury to speak about it as historical rather than active. The conversation does not need to produce reconciliation in the romantic sense; it needs to produce *mutual acknowledgment* — her of the harm, his of the conviction. The structure of moral injury is that the injured party is unable to forgive themselves; the only external input that meaningfully shifts this is the wronged party's expressed understanding (not forgiveness — *understanding*). Hank is, on his own evidence, capable of this. The question is whether they arrive in the same room with the same readiness, which is a matter of timing she does not control.

2. **A second Legacy-structure dilemma resolved more slowly.** Not differently, necessarily — she may well make the same call, and there are scenarios in which the same call is right. But resolved with *deliberation*, with consultation, with the prior warning to the affected intimate that she did not give the first time. The diagnostic is not the outcome; it is the *process*. Slower process means the first time was an injury she has learned from, not a script she is doomed to rerun.

3. **Generative transmission.** Naming, to a successor, what the Legacy disclosure cost and what it bought, in the same sentence, without flinching from either half. This is the act that converts the wound into wisdom — not by resolving it but by making it usable to someone else. It is the closest thing to peace her structure allows.

If all three occur, Subject ends her life as one of the rare figures in her corpus who has integrated rather than survived. The integration would be visible in small things: less compulsive work hours, a re-expanded social field, an ability to be in a room with Hank without the room going still, a willingness to write the book under her own name and her own face rather than as a third-person retrospective.

The probability of all three occurring in the available window is **low but not negligible**. Call it fifteen percent on current evidence.

---

### 4. The Catastrophe Vector

Catastrophe, for Subject, does not look like collapse. Her ego strength precludes the dramatic decompensations that befall less-organized characters in her orbit. Catastrophe looks like *the calcification completing* — the wound becoming the entire architecture, the person reducing to the role, the inner life shrinking to a maintenance loop.

The mechanism runs through Forks F and G in some combination, possibly accelerated by Fork C in its vindication form.

The sequence:

1. **Platform loss in her late fifties.** The industry contracts; the beat she built no longer commands the resources it did; she is offered a buyout or a diminished role and takes the buyout because the diminished role is more humiliating than the exit. She freelances. The freelance work is good. It is not enough to bind the affect.

2. **Hank's death** — in the line of work, in the slow erosion of his secondary-mutation physiology, in something unspectacular — before any reconciliation conversation has occurred. She learns of it through the wire she used to file to. She does not attend the service; she is not on the list, and putting herself on it would require asking. She writes the obituary that runs in her former outlet, anonymously, and it is the best thing written about him. Nobody knows she wrote it. This is the moment the catastrophe vector becomes irreversible.

3. **The contracted late period.** Work continues at reduced volume; the inner ring shrinks to one or two; she becomes the kind of private that is indistinguishable from absence. She is not depressed in the clinical sense. She is *vacated*. The moral injury has consumed the available oxygen of the personality and left the competence intact and the rest hollowed.

4. **A long, dignified, lonely end.** No drama. No precipitating crisis. The obituaries lead with Legacy. She would have wanted them to lead with something else and would have died not having found out what.

The probability of this trajectory on current evidence is **moderate**. Call it thirty-five percent. It is the modal failure mode for her type.

The remaining fifty percent is the baseline above — the calcified-but-functional late life, neither growth nor catastrophe, the long quiet survival that is the most common outcome for high-functioning adults carrying unhealed wounds.

---

### 5. Open Questions

A surveillance file is partly defined by what it does not yet know. The questions an intelligence apparatus would actively monitor on Subject:

- **Has she written anything about Legacy under her own name?** A book, a long essay, an on-the-record interview. The absence of this in the record to date is itself a data point; its eventual presence (or its continued absence into her sixties) is the most reliable single signal of which trajectory she is on. The growth vector requires the writing; the catastrophe vector forbids it; the baseline produces a posthumous draft found in a drawer.

- **Does she keep anything of Hank's?** A surveillance file would want to know what is on her shelves, what is in the box at the back of the closet, whether the photographs are out or away or destroyed. The somatic relationship to the artifacts of the relationship is the most honest readout of the internal state, and she has revealed nothing of it on-record. The inference from her defense profile (intellectualization-dominant, no projection, no splitting) is that the artifacts are *kept* and *not displayed* — boxed, accessible, unvisited. This is the most diagnostic possible answer; visit-frequency would refine it.

- **Has she ever, after the disclosure, deliberately *not* run a story she could have run?** A single instance of professional suppression in service of a personal loyalty would be the largest single behavioral inversion available to her. The record does not show one. Its eventual appearance — or its continued non-appearance — discriminates sharply between growth and repetition.

- **What is her relationship to her own aging?** No data in record. Whether she dyes the gray, whether she still goes to the scene when she can justify it, whether she has begun the late-career inventory work or is actively avoiding it. A file would want clinic visits, hair appointments, gym membership cadence; the trivia is the index.

- **Who is her emergency contact?** The single most informative line in any file on a person living without a partner. Mother, if alive. A sister, if she has one. A producer. Hank, never updated since 1994, still on a form somewhere she has not thought to revise. Each answer rotates the assessment.

- **Does she read his work?** He publishes; he is a scientist of record. A subscription to a journal, a copy of a paper on a desk, a search history. If yes: the wound is tended, not closed. If no: the wound is walled, not healed. Either confirms unresolution; the distinction is in the texture of the unresolution.

- **What is the dream content?** Unavailable to standard surveillance, but the question stands. Subjects carrying unresolved moral injury characteristically dream the wronged party's face. The frequency and the affective tone of those dreams over time is the truest available curve of the inner state. A clinician would ask. A file would not get the answer.

---

### 6. Single-Likeliest Path

Synthesizing the above:

Subject's most probable next decade is the **calcifying baseline**. She continues at platform for another five to eight years, transitions to a senior analyst or long-form role, narrows further socially, does not partner, mentors one or two junior reporters seriously, and does not seek the conversation with Hank that her structure requires for resolution. The wound holds steady at its current depth; the personality continues to organize around it; she remains high-functioning and quietly diminished.

The most probable disruption to that baseline is **Fork E** — the mentorship that turns into a Legacy-structure consultation. This is the fork most consistent with her actual late-career position (she *is* now senior enough to be asked) and the one that requires the least external action by parties she does not control (Hank, the industry, her own body). It is the fork at which growth becomes available through an act she can initiate: telling someone younger the true thing about the cost.

Whether she takes that fork is the entire question.

The assessment is that she **probably does**, partially, late, and with characteristic understatement — not the full integration described in the growth vector, but a partial transmission, a half-conversation, a sentence said once that the mentee remembers for thirty years. This is consistent with her defensive profile (mature, intellectualizing, conviction-preserving) and with the slow-motion grace of her record to date. It is not resolution. It is the maximum movement her structure permits without the external inputs she cannot summon.

Final read: she will not heal. She will become useful to someone else's healing. For a person of her ethical seriousness, this is not a consolation prize. It is the form her flourishing was always going to take, if it took any form at all.

The file remains open.

## Relationship Graph
### [[Henry Philip McCoy (Beast)]]
- Primary romantic partner across X-Factor mid-run; relationship initiates while he is in de-mutated human form.
- Sustained the bond across his re-mutation into furred/leonine/simian iterations - the first hard disconfirmation of the 'shallow' read.
- Ruptured by the Legacy Virus broadcast: information given in private/relational confidence converted to on-air dispatch under public-health framing.
- Attempted reconciliation post-rupture; failed.
- Current state: civil professional intersection, no retaliation, no exposé despite operational knowledge of X-secrets - a hard rule.
- Failure mode (active): the structure that produced the leak is unrevised; under analogous stakes, she would do it again. Bedrock loyalty is NOT restorable on her current terms.
- Leverage: he is the one person whose patient, non-hostile inquiry could still reach the unworked seam - which makes him both the lever and the person least likely to pull it.

### X Factor Team
- Long-term beat coverage; mix of professional source relationships and earned trust.
- Will help when help and story align; will not subordinate story to team interest.
- Leverage: appeal to scale - offer a larger frame than the one she's working in.

### X Men General
- Recognized press presence on the mutant beat; treated as functionally trustworthy on a per-story basis.
- Operational knowledge of secrets she has chosen not to publish - a stability built on her non-retaliation rule, not on suppression.
- Failure mode: a sufficiently large public-health or public-safety story implicating them would re-trigger the Legacy pattern.

### Network Employer
- Functional, transactional, mutually instrumental.
- Leverage: assignment is the lever; pulling her off the mutant beat would corrode her faster than any personal pressure.

### Anti Mutant Political Figures
- Adversarial sources, handled with practiced aggression.
- She will quote them accurately, contextualize them devastatingly, and not pretend to neutrality on the basic question of mutant personhood.
- Leverage on her from their side: accusations of bias - the one frame that genuinely destabilizes self-concept.
